The Rickshaw Problem is Serious: The Management Committee Refuses to Issue New Licenses 120

Rickshaw Owners Were Refused Licenses at the Vehicle Inspection Office Yesterday Morning

The Trade Association Appeals to Various Organizations for Assistance in Negotiations

Xinxin News Agency reports that the public concession rickshaw problem is due to the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Management Committee's scheduled implementation of new regulations, and the rickshaw owners firmly oppose them because the burden is too heavy, creating a confrontation between the two sides. One hundred and forty-four rickshaw owners in the special zone went to the Gongping Road Vehicle Inspection Office yesterday morning to collect new licenses in accordance with the past licensing methods, but were refused issuance, making the situation more serious. It is speculated that if both sides continue to be extreme, then unfortunate events will occur in the near future. The details learned by the Xinxin News Agency reporters are recorded below.

Starting to Collect Licenses: Representatives of 144 rickshaw owners in the special zone went to the rickshaw inspection office to collect the vehicle inspection qualification certificate in accordance with the Municipal Council's regulations for decades, so that they could pay the donation to the Municipal Council's Donation Office and collect the August business license in order to do business. At 9:40 am yesterday morning, they gathered at the Special Zone Office of the Rickshaw Trade Association on Lloyd Road, led by rickshaw owner Gu Songmao and others, and took six moving trucks to the Gongping Road Vehicle Inspection Office to collect new licenses.

Refusal to Issue: After the rickshaw owners arrived at the vehicle inspection office, ten representatives were sent to request the issuance of new licenses so that they could pay the donation and collect the licenses for business. Director Si Huangjun (transliteration) received them and said that the office had received a rejection, etc.

Requesting Assistance: The rickshaw industry association, according to reports from the rickshaw owners, believes that the association intends to destroy the industry, so it decided to handle it in accordance with the resolution of the general meeting, depositing the donations to be paid in the bank, and sending letters to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Taxpayers Association, and the Municipal Council's Director-General for assistance. The original letter is recorded below: Respectfully submitted, rickshaw owners have been operating the rickshaw industry for 50 years, inheriting it from generation to generation. They have been holding licenses from the Municipal Council, paying donations monthly, and contributing tens of thousands of dollars annually. The rickshaw regulations have always taken into account the obligations and rights of the rickshaw industry, so the rickshaw owners have been able to follow them carefully and have not changed them. Unexpectedly, due to the establishment of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, all the previous regulations have been suddenly changed, and all of them are matters that cannot be followed. It seems that there are only obligations and no rights to speak of, and rickshaw owners are urged to directly collect licenses starting in August, which is even more incomprehensible. 1. It is found that the method of issuing licenses has always been that a small number of vehicles are donated on behalf of those with a larger number of vehicles, and the license applicant is required to prepare a store guarantee or cash on file. Now, without announcing the termination of liability and returning the certificate money, the rickshaw owners who donate on behalf of others are suddenly ordered to directly collect licenses. This is incomprehensible. 2. Rickshaws in the public concession travel throughout the three zones, so they should donate three zone licenses. However, the three zone licenses are all donated on behalf of others. This is a very systematic method of collecting licenses, which has been convenient for rickshaw owners and the authorities have easy procedures and no objections. Now, although the Municipal Council wants to order each to donate and collect licenses, the other two zones still need to be donated on behalf of others, which makes the rickshaw owners feel more troublesome in the procedures. This is incomprehensible. 3. Regarding the registered rickshaw owners, the names are not announced in advance, and the donor is not allowed to prove it. Only the rickshaw owner's self-registration is taken as the standard, and they are allowed to issue certificates and collect licenses based on the certificate. It is found that there are many genuine rickshaw owners living in other places. At this time, it is difficult to guarantee that there are no fake registrants. Even the certificates now state that "according to the rickshaw owner's claim, it is assumed temporarily," etc. And each rickshaw owner sent 180 rickshaw owner certificates issued by our committee, and there are more than 30 names that are wrong, totaling more than 177 vehicles. There are more than 700 lower joint certificates that have not been issued, and it is even more difficult to count the number of errors among them. How will disputes be resolved in the future? This is incomprehensible. 4. The Municipal Council originally ordered the rickshaw license regulations to be issued every three months as a means of collecting licenses on time. The autumn certificate has already been issued, noting that the valid period is July, August, and September. Suddenly, it changed in the middle, and only July can execute this license, and it will not take effect after that. This is incomprehensible. Based on the above reasons, the rickshaw owners are facing difficulties in the new regulations, strict old system, and unnecessary changes. The rickshaw owners have been donating for many years, and it is now the time to collect licenses in August. It is not a small matter that it is related to the Municipal Council's donation collection, the rickshaw owners' business, and the rickshaw pullers' livelihoods. Therefore, a special document is submitted to Junzuo (your association) for verification. All August vehicle licenses (please ask the Municipal Council) allow the rickshaw owners to still donate and collect licenses as before in order to maintain the rickshaw industry and to benefit the lives of more than 100,000 rickshaw pullers and their families. It is for the public good.

Remarks by Standing Committee Members of the Postal Service Associations 130

Problem of Overdrafts for Telegraphs from Postal Savings

Regarding the "Contract for Agency Collection and Payment of Funds and the Overdraft Loan for Long-Distance Telephone in Nine Provinces and Jiangsu Province" recently concluded between the Ministry of Communications and the General Bureau of Postal Savings and Remittances, the Shanghai Postal Service Association and the Postal Workers' Association, in the interest of the safety of public savings, considered it inappropriate to have substantial overdrafts from postal savings for the telegraph bureau without effective guarantees. Therefore, they jointly telegraphed the Ministry a few days ago to request rectification to protect the interests of public savings. However, the remarks made by the person in charge of the Ministry of Communications and Mr. Xu Baiyuan of the local Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau denied the substantial overdrafts. Yesterday, committee members of the two postal service associations stated that postal savings are accumulated from the small amounts of hard-earned savings of the public, so the government has specifically enacted the Postal Savings Law, with particularly careful management. In addition to the contract for agency collection and payment of funds concluded between the Telegraph Administration of the Ministry of Communications and the General Bureau of Postal Savings and Remittances, there is also a contract for overdraft loans with ten articles, of which articles 5, 6, 7, 8, and 10 have not been announced, and their contents are unknown, which is cause for concern. However, according to reports from various places, such as Zhejiang Province's total revenue from telegram and telephone charges in July was 3,216.07 yuan, while the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau paid out 11,252 yuan for telegraphs. Changsha's revenue was 8,000 yuan, while its payments were 12,000 yuan. Jinan, Shandong's revenue from wired and wireless telegram charges was 9,000 yuan, while its expenditures were 15,000 yuan. In addition, Qingdao's expenditures for wired and wireless telegrams were 15,600 yuan, and Yantai's telegraph expenditures were 12,000 yuan, while its telephone charges were 3,200 yuan. Tianjin receives a subsidy of 50,000 yuan each month from the Savings and Remittances Bureau for the telegraph bureau, and Beijing receives 120,000 yuan in July. The above only represents a small portion of the revenue and expenditures nationwide, and the amount of overdrafts is already so large. If calculated nationwide, the so-called overdraft of 500,000 yuan per month is definitely unfounded. However, according to Mr. Xu Baiyuan of the Savings and Remittances Bureau, he also admitted that the contract stipulates that the Telegraph Administration can overdraft 100,000 yuan, yet he falsely accused the telegram from the two associations of being groundless, which is self-contradictory. In short, the two associations, in order to protect the interests of public savings due to the inappropriate nature of the contract, have petitioned the Ministry of Communications to pay attention, which is their duty. However, in his remarks, Mr. Xu's attitude towards the two associations was arrogant and his language was rude, only demeaning himself. The two associations do not wish to argue with him.

Committee members present: Zhang Xiaoyan, Yang Xuemen, Xue Liansheng, Lin Bingyu, Shi Yitang, Ye Chengtai, Jiang Shude, Xu Ziqin, Xu Fang, Chen Fusheng, Cheng Zuoqing, Zhang Dianjia, Wang Kai, Lu Keming, Zhang Xiyang, Zhang Guangshu, He Tingjia, Wang Shaohua, Wu Yanbin, Fan Caicong, Zhang Kechang, Cao Chongye, Xu Duo, Liu Xinquan, Ge Fei, Liang Shaodong, Shui Xiangyun, Zhu Jingsheng, Huang Gongfu, Chen Shengyang, Gao Zhicheng, and Shen Songzhou, Xiao Qingshan. Committee members attending ex officio: Zhao Shusheng, Lu Jingshi, and Zhu Xuefan. Chairman: Chen Shengyang. Recorder: Xiao Qingshan. 1. Formalities were observed. 2. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting, stating briefly that the recent joint postal and telegraph setup and the contract for agency collection and payment of telegrams by the General Bureau of Postal Savings and Remittances are affecting the postal service's economy, and the plan to consolidate the postal foundation has not yet been implemented, so this joint meeting of the two associations is specifically convened to discuss and implement measures. 3. Chen Shengyang and Zhang Kechang reported on recent developments. 4. Committee member Zhao Shusheng reported on the deduction of union dues by the authorities in the bandit suppression areas of five provinces and the negotiations with the National Postal Workers' General Union. 5. Matters for discussion: (1) The Ministry of Communications, during the trial period of the joint postal and telegraph setup, the General Bureau of Postal Savings and Remittances and the Telegraph Administration concluded a contract for the postal service to collect and pay for telegrams, and the postal savings authorities stated that they could overdraft 100,000 yuan per month. This measure violates the principle of independent postal economics and harms the interests of postal savings depositors. In order to maintain postal economics and ensure the safety of savings, how should this be expressed for public decision? Resolved: A. The joint postal and telegraph setup violates the principle of independent economics, so a petition should be submitted to the Ministry of Communications to suspend it. B. The postal and telegraph revenue and expenditure contract lacks effective guarantees for overdrafts, which hinders the safety of savings. A petition should be submitted to the Ministry of Communications to cancel the revenue and expenditure contract, carefully manage the use of postal savings, maintain postal credit, and protect public savings. (2) Regarding the case of merging savings and remittance bureaus, which has been passed by the Legislative Yuan but has not yet been implemented, how should it proceed? Resolved: A. A report should be submitted to the Central Political Council to promptly review and implement the original plan passed by the Legislative Yuan. B. A report should be submitted to the Legislative Yuan to request detailed information and to forward it to the Central Political Council for prompt review and approval. (3) Recently, it was reported that the postal authorities announced a postal deficit of over ten million yuan, while in the 23rd accounting year, the post office still subsidized airlines by more than 1.4 million yuan, increasing the postal deficit. The Ministry of Communications should be requested to immediately stop the subsidy in accordance with the decision of the Postal Economics System Research Committee. Resolved: Passed. (4) The postal service has been established for more than thirty years, with unified authority and all facilities operating in accordance with the orders of the communications authorities. However, the Ministry of Communications has decided to convene a national postal conference in the capital on September 1, and the purpose of the conference is unknown. Moreover, this conference is related to the entire postal service and is very important, but employee organizations have not been invited to participate. How should this be expressed? Resolved: Request the Ministry of Communications to announce the purpose of the meeting and request permission to send representatives to participate in the meeting. (5) Recently, in the bandit suppression areas of five provinces, the postal authorities suddenly stopped deducting postal union dues, which hinders postal transportation. How should this be handled? Resolved: A. A petition should be submitted to the Ministry of Communications, firmly requesting that the post office be ordered to deduct dues as usual. B. A telegram should be sent to Chairman Chiang, explaining the special circumstances of the postal union and that dues should be collected as usual. (6) (7) Not announced. (8) How should the above resolutions be handled? Resolved: Handed over to the standing committees of the two associations for active handling. 6. Meeting adjourned.

The Municipal Government Instructs the Social Affairs Bureau to Suppress the Private Issuance of Currency 132

The Shanghai Municipal Government instructed the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating, "The Ministry of Finance's document Qian Zi No. 6258 states that in the resolution presented by the secretariat of the National Finance Conference, member Xu Kan proposed suppressing the private minting of silver and copper coins and the private issuance of paper money in order to purify the currency system. After review, it was deemed essential and proposed that the Ministry, in accordance with existing laws and regulations, inform the provinces to effectively suppress it. The examination opinion was submitted, and the fourth general meeting resolved to adopt the examination opinion. The central government has already made overall plans and established a framework for currency consolidation, and the provinces and cities must cooperate and assist in earnest execution to ensure compliance with central government policies to achieve synergistic results. The Ministry has previously ordered provincial mints to destroy old dies and has repeatedly ordered provincial and municipal governments to strictly suppress private minting and issuance. However, some local governments still have privately established minting institutions or privately open furnaces in existing mints to mint silver coins, silver dollars, and copper coins. Local banks, money shops, and businesses still privately issue paper money for exchange of silver dollars and copper coins or similar paper vouchers, which seriously hinders the unification of the currency system, disrupts financial stability, and harms the local area. The National Finance Conference, recognizing this, proposed suppressing private minting and issuance to purify the currency system. Resolved: The Ministry should, in accordance with existing laws and regulations, inform the provinces to effectively suppress it. The Ministry should follow this resolution and instruct the municipal government to investigate whether banks, money shops, and businesses within its jurisdiction are privately printing and issuing paper money for exchange of silver dollars and copper coins or similar paper vouchers. If such paper money exists, it should be redeemed, recovered, and destroyed within three months of receiving the document, and no further issuance should be allowed. Regarding the suppression of private minting of silver and copper coins, the municipal government should investigate whether there are privately established mints or existing mints privately opening furnaces to mint silver and copper coins. If such private minting exists, it should be ordered to cease minting within one month of receiving the document, and the dies should be sent to the Ministry for verification and destruction. Regarding the above two items, it is hoped that the municipal government will cooperate and assist in earnest execution. If this can be achieved, it will not only alleviate the people's suffering but also greatly benefit the administrative power. In addition to separate notifications, a corresponding notification is hereby issued for investigation, instruction to subordinates to comply, and a report on the suppression situation is requested to be submitted at any time."

Commemoration of the Second Anniversary of the Commercial Press's Resumption of Business 134

1,200 New Books Sold at Half Price

Held for Two Months from August 1st

The Commercial Press of this city has been in operation for two years since its resumption of business. Its production capacity has been restored, and all the books destroyed in the January 28th Shanghai Incident have generally been reprinted. More than 1,000 new books have also been published since the resumption of business. To commemorate this, over 1,200 newly reprinted and newly published books are being offered at half price for two months. The half-price books cover all subjects (including 10 dictionaries and thesauruses) and are displayed gradually. Sales are limited to in-person or mail-order purchases, and each person is limited to one copy of each title. This half-price offer is uniformly applied at the Shanghai main branch and all branch offices. The publishing house and the three branches on Jing'an Temple Road, Xiafei Road, and Hongkou in this city have been scheduled to hold the event from August 1st and will display over 300 half-price books in the first week. According to an employee of the publishing house, the publishing house usually sells inexpensive books at around 20% off, and most of them are local sales. The fact that the new books offered this time are as many as 1,000 or more and are all sold at half price is unprecedented. In addition, with 500 copies of each discounted book, the total sacrifice of the publishing house for this commemorative half-price sale amounts to tens of thousands of yuan. From the perspective of the reading public, it can save tens of thousands of yuan in book prices, which is an excellent opportunity to purchase and read new books.

Japanese Newspaper Reports Booming Japanese Goods Exports to China 135

Combining Various Reasons

Not Only Due to Relaxed Boycott

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun reported on the 26th that, since the surprising leap in trade with Manchuria, trade with China has been very weak due to various reasons. However, since the second half of the year, all shipping routes have suddenly become active. The Jing Shan Maru, which departed from Osaka on the 24th on the Dagu-Kobe-Tianjin line, loaded 1,000 tons of rice in Kobe, 450 tons of sugar in Osaka, Kobe, and Moji, and 300 tons of printing paper. The round trips of the Beiling Maru are always full of exports. Other shipping lines, such as the shipping company's sea line, are also actively exporting sugar and cotton. This situation has not been seen in the past two or three years. The reasons for this are: (1) China's revised tariffs have reduced tax rates and removed trade uncertainties; (2) The restoration of Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations has eased and eliminated the rejection of Japanese goods; (3) Sino-Japanese exchange rates have stabilized; (4) The strike of dockworkers in the North Pacific has halted US trade with China, which is sufficient to increase Japanese goods exports to China.

The Luggage Swindled at the North Station Belongs to Chen Qingwen 141

The China Travel Service of This City Claims

The Person Who Came Impersonated a Servant of Song Ziwen

The China Travel Service sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, stating, "Dear Sir, We have read the news item in today's issue of your newspaper, 'A Travelling Companion's Two Small Leather Suitcases Lost.' Upon investigation, the luggage in question was entirely consigned by Director Chen Qingwen of the Beining Railway Bureau and was absolutely not the property of Director Yin. We are now providing a detailed account of the actual circumstances of the loss of four of the items and hope that you will grant us a correction to clarify the facts and avoid confusing the listeners: On the 28th of this month, Mr. Chen Qingwen, Director of the Traffic Department of the Beining Railway, returned to Shanghai by ship 'Lai Pula' after completing his private affairs in Singapore, bringing 24 pieces of luggage with him. That night, he entrusted them to our company to be sent directly from the wharf to the station for transport to Tianjin. Except for 20 of them, which were tagged and loaded onto the baggage car according to regulations, the remaining two pieces of food and two small leather suitcases were intended to be carried by Mr. Chen as carry-on luggage. About half an hour before the departure of the night train, a person resembling a servant suddenly approached our North Station reception desk and claimed to have been sent by the Song Ziwen residence to greet Director Chen and asked about the number of Director Chen's berth on the train. At that time, our receptionist did not suspect anything and accompanied the luggage to the train and temporarily placed it in room 508. The receptionist then got off the train to perform his duties. About five minutes before the departure, the receptionist, not seeing Director Chen arrive at the station, rushed back to the train to check on the luggage. According to the train attendant, the servant claimed that room 508 was reserved for Mr. Chen Weiqing and not for Director Chen, so he moved the four pieces of luggage to another sleeping car. The receptionist then searched all the rooms for the luggage without success, and the departure time had arrived, so he had to get off the train and search for it at various stations along the way, but without finding any clues. He also inquired at the Song residence and learned that no servants had been sent to the station. Therefore, the luggage must have been swindled and lost. Our company is now making every effort to investigate in the hope of uncovering the truth." China Travel Service.

Brother-in-Law Helps Sister-in-Law Argue, Chops Creditor to Death 143

Li Shuqing Demands Debt Payment, Zheng Bei Starts Trouble

Song Yongfa Surrenders to Police Station After Committing the Crime

Li Shuqing, a 31-year-old resident of Shanghai from Tianjin, residing at No. 22, Sandeli, Lujiazui, Pudong, made a living working in an elevator at a certain company. His wife remained in their hometown with his father, farming. Recently, Li's father sent his daughter-in-law to Shanghai but wanted to return to his hometown alone. Li, facing financial difficulties and lacking travel expenses, remembered that his cousin Song Yongfa's sister-in-law, Song Songshi, had borrowed several yuan from him in the past. So, around 9 PM the previous evening, he went to Song's home at No. 12, Wufu Alley, to demand repayment to cover his father's travel expenses back home. Song had no money to repay at the time, and the two began to argue. Song Yongfa, the sister-in-law’s uncle, lived in the same house and was already asleep. Hearing the noise, he came out to help his sister-in-law argue. Neither side would yield. Li, in a fit of anger, threw a teacup at Yongfa's head, breaking his forehead. Yongfa, in a sudden rage, grabbed a noodle-cutting knife about two feet long and, without asking the reason, violently chopped at Li's right neck, penetrating two inches deep. His trachea severed, Li fell to the ground, dying instantly. Yongfa, realizing the gravity of the crime, immediately took the murder weapon and surrendered to the police officer on duty. The police took his sister-in-law, Songshi, and the deceased's uncle, Song Fujin, to the police station's Third Squad, which transferred them to the Third District. After District Chief Zhang inquired about the cause, he ordered the uncle and sister-in-law to be detained. Yesterday morning, he ordered the local guarantor, Lu Shunlong, to petition the local court. At 2 PM, Inspector Kong was appointed to go to Pudong to examine the body. The body was handed over to the deceased's father for funeral arrangements. The two defendants and the murder weapon were taken to the court for interrogation.

Water Company Increases Price of Fire Hydrant Water 144

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council to Stop It

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Director-General of the Municipal Council yesterday, which stated: "Sir, according to a letter from the accounting department of the Sanxin Company, 'Our company has three fire hydrants installed at the Rongchangli houses on Dongyouheng Road. We pay a water fee of 3.75 yuan per quarter, calculated at a 60% discount of the original price of 6.25 yuan. This water is installed for public safety. Usually we do not use even a tiny amount of it. Now we have received a letter from the water company stating that a new contract must be signed for these hydrants, with a price of 6.25 yuan each, totaling 18.75 yuan per quarter for three, which is more than a fivefold increase. Before the contract is signed, they are temporarily charging 80% of 6.25 yuan per hydrant, which is 15 yuan per quarter for three, still a fourfold increase. When we inquired about the reason, they said that if all houses use the company's water, the old price can be paid (i.e., 3.75 yuan per quarter for three). Our company uses its own well water and must follow the new contract.' Their intention is clearly coercion. If Shanghai does not use the company's water materials, why should we be at their mercy? Moreover, the installation of fire hydrants is a water company monopoly and cannot be compared to other businesses. Profiting in this way may seriously affect public safety. We have always admired your council as the voice of the people, especially enthusiastic in handling social affairs. Therefore, we dare to state the facts as above, and hope that you will raise an objection. We would be most grateful.' This matter has reached the Association. The Association believes that the installation of fire hydrants is intended to prevent fires. The regular fee should only be called installation or maintenance fee. The water used to extinguish fires should certainly be charged. This has nothing to do with the use of household water from wells and is completely unrelated to whether or not tap water is used. Now, the charging difference is based on the distinction between household well water and tap water. We do not know under what legal or human rationale this regulation is based. It is appropriate to say it is 'nothing but coercion.' Accordingly, we are writing to request your bureau to instruct the water company to cancel this discrimination as necessary."

Second Shipment Currently Being Planned

Many Difficulties Exist, Requiring Immediate Remedies

The Fruit Industry Association of this city, recognizing that the quality of fruit produced in our country is excellent, but foreigners rarely buy and eat it due to a lack of promotion, deems it necessary to find ways to promote it abroad to expand the overseas market. Therefore, this spring, a large batch of Tianjin pears, chestnuts, ginkgo nuts, dried dates, and other fruits were shipped to Liverpool, England, for a trial sale. Yesterday, according to the person in charge of the Association, most of the first batch of goods shipped to Liverpool, England, for trial sale have been sold out, and the British highly praised them. The second batch of goods is being planned, and besides Tianjin pears which still need further promotion, there may be slight changes to the other goods. Regarding the difficulties in selling abroad, the first is the lack of overseas postal ships from our country, and the high cost of loading and unloading foreign ships is truly alarming. In fact, merchants simply cannot afford it, making it difficult for the price of our fruit to compete with foreign fruits. Secondly, the long distances make the fruit easily spoiled, resulting in heavy losses. Currently, if our country's fruit industry needs to gain a market abroad, the government should provide full assistance to alleviate shipping costs as the first point of difficulty. Merchants can find their own remedies for the second point of difficulty, it is said.

Debt Collection Leads to Murder 149

Debtor Li Shuqing Chopped to Death

Creditor Song Yongfa Arrested for the Crime

Li Shuqing, a Tianjin native residing at No. 12, Wufu Alley, Yanchang Road, Lujiazhai, Pudong, had previously borrowed dozens of yuan from Song Yongfa, a relative who lived in the same house and cut paper, due to financial difficulties. He had not yet repaid it. At 9:20 PM the previous evening, Song demanded repayment of the debt. Li, unable to repay it at that time, caused a dispute. Initially, it was just a verbal argument at Li's house, but due to disagreement, it turned into a physical fight between the two. Li first threw a rice bowl at Song, hitting him in the forehead and causing profuse bleeding. Realizing that he had caused trouble, he fled in fear of punishment. Song, harboring resentment, took a knife and chased him to the door. When Li turned to resist, he was accurately struck on the right side of his neck with a fierce chop. The wound was quite deep. He collapsed instantly, dying on the spot. The deceased's uncle, Song Fuqin, reported the incident to Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He immediately ordered Patrol Officer and Detective Team Leader Li Youbao, stationed in the Third District, along with detectives Jiang Binru and Chen Jinshan, to rush to the scene of the incident with the No. 6 patrol officer. They arrested the murderer, Song Yongfa, and his sister-in-law, Song Songshi, and took them to the district for detention. After a brief interrogation at the bureau this morning, District Chief Zhang, considering the case involved a death, ordered that a document be prepared to send the Song defendants to Section 3 of the main bureau for legal action this afternoon. At the same time, he instructed the local guarantor to request the local court to inspect and collect the body.

Li Jianyun Secretly Signed a Divorce Agreement Before His Death 151

His Wife Demanded 50,000 Yuan Before Agreeing to Divorce

Li's Wife, née Lu, Published a Denial in the Newspaper After the Matter Was Exposed

Li Jianyun, a native of Nanhui, Pudong, and the owner of the Chuntai Cooperative Construction Company at No. 810, the corner of Xiaoshadu Road and Haifang Road, unexpectedly shot and wounded his beloved concubine, Chen Zhanlian, the previous morning. Chen Zhanlian died from her wounds. He then committed suicide. Neither survived. After receiving the report, the Gordon Road police dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. The bodies were sent to the Fellen Road morgue for autopsy. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that Li had a legal wife named Lu Lingxian, with whom he had four children, all living with their mother in their hometown. Last year, after Li began an affair with Chen and cohabited with her, he planned to abandon Lu and marry Chen as his official wife. However, Lu demanded 50,000 yuan before agreeing to a divorce, while Li was only willing to give 5,000 yuan. The difference was too great, and it was not implemented. In November of last year, Li went to lawyer Sun Zuji several times, falsely claiming that he had paid Lu 3,000 yuan and agreed to a divorce. On the 17th of that month, he took two seals, his own and Lu's, and asked lawyer Sun to certify an agreement of divorce. But in April of this year, the matter was exposed, and Lu immediately published a denial in the newspaper. As a result, the plan to marry Chen never materialized. On the 27th of this month, Chen suddenly received a letter from her brother, Chen Moqian, urging her to marry Li. Both of them must have had unspeakable pain in their hearts, which led to this tragedy. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court received the report and dispatched Inspector Tang Peiyou, along with two forensic doctors, Wei Qiu and Wang Zuyi, to the scene to verify the bodies. According to Li Xianglin, the deceased Li Jianyun was his brother, previously a pattern maker and currently unemployed, residing in his hometown. Recently, he came to Shanghai for medical treatment because of illness and stayed in the hospital. Chen Zhanlian was deeply loved by his brother. Recently, Chen's brother wanted to persuade them to marry, which may have led to this unfortunate event. He now requests that his brother's body be given to him for collection, and Chen's body will be claimed by her nephew. According to Zhao Zhou, a servant in the Li family, around 8 AM this morning, she went upstairs to fetch a chamber pot and saw that the young master had already gotten up, while the young mistress was still lying in bed. So, she hurried to fetch washing water. At that time, she did not see any movement. Later, she went downstairs and suddenly heard a gunshot, but she couldn't tell what it was and thought something had happened on the road, so she didn't go to look. Later, the chauffeur brought a piece of paper, saying that he wanted to get gasoline and asked her to ask the young master to sign it. Only then did she discover that both of them were lying in pools of blood. She reported it to the police. According to Du Yingxi, the deceased Chen Zhanlian was his aunt, and he was willing to claim the body. After the Chinese and foreign detectives reported the above situation, Tang 君 ordered that the deceased Li Jianyun, male, and the deceased Chen Zhanlian, female, both died from gunshot wounds sustained during their lifetime. The male body was handed over to Li Xianglin, and the female body was handed over to Du Yingxi, with separate guarantees to claim them back for coffin burial.

Although Madame Wu, also known as Ergou, is middle-aged, her charm has not diminished. Her name is known to almost everyone in the Cantonese community. Wu is exceptionally skilled, and the prostitutes she keeps are all beauties. The villa is decorated with extreme opulence, so patrons flock to it like geese, and they are all high-ranking officials, wealthy merchants, and comprador of foreign firms. Therefore, over the years, Ergou has accumulated a lot of wealth and has retired from prostitution. She has become acquainted with a large real estate merchant and acts only as a procuress. On the 20th of this month, Wu Genyuan, the inspector of the Public Concession Western District Police, learned of the situation and ordered his subordinates to arrest Ergou and several prostitutes and send them to the First Special Court for sentencing. After Ergou was released from detention, she became more secretive but continued to operate the prostitution business in secret. Unexpectedly, at 10 PM the day before yesterday, Chinese Detective Wen Youheng of the Hongkou Police Station went to raid the villa with a search warrant from the First Special Court. At that time, there were three patrons inside having fun. All three were from Guangdong. One of them could only speak English and not Chinese, and seemed to be an overseas Chinese. One was rumored to be a comprador of a certain bank. The detective arrested Ergou and five prostitutes: Wang A'mei, Lu A'zhen, Chen A'mei, Zhu A'zhen, and Chen Liu'mei. The sixth prostitute, Liu'mei, was richly dressed and beautiful. All six were taken back to the police station and transferred to the women's prison. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special Court, and were charged with violations of Article 36 of the Municipal Council Bylaws and Article 43 of the Police Penalty Law. After Detective Wen explained the circumstances of the arrest, interrogations of Ergou revealed cunning lies. Wang A'mei and Lu A'zhen claimed to be dancers who were visiting sisters yesterday. Chen A'mei and others claimed to be servants. Judge Shen checked their fingerprints and discovered that both Ergou and Chen A'mei had been fined for prostitution before, so they could not lie. He sentenced Wu Ergou to a fine of 15 yuan and the rest to 10 yuan as a warning.

No Lounging Allowed on Xinzha Bridge 152

Xinzha Bridge connects the Concession in the south with the Chinese territory of Zhabei in the north, making it an important thoroughfare between the Chinese and Concession territories. After the Lu-Qi War in 1914, the authorities found that the sidewalks on both sides of the bridge were dangerous. To prevent accidents, the sidewalks were removed, leaving only the center of the bridge, and heavy vehicles are still not allowed to pass. Since the beginning of summer this year, the weather has been hot, and small vendors and laborers, who live in cramped rooms, cannot sleep well at night, so they all lounge on the bridge to cool off. They are repeatedly driven away and return. To avoid accidents, District Chief Gong has specially posted a notice saying, "The bridge is narrow, and vehicles are dangerous. No lounging on the bridge."

Verdict in the Case of Lye Splashed on Dancer 153

Huang Naiwu and Jiang Ada Each Sentenced to Ten Months' Imprisonment

Huang Naiwu, a 22-year-old university student from Jiangxi, had a grudge against Li Xiuying (also known as Gui Zhen, 21 years old this year), a dancer from the Da Hu Dance Hall on Haige Road in Tianjin. On June 20, Huang bought a bottle of nitric acid and incited Jiang Ada, a Suzhou native he knew, to splash the acid on Li at the Da Hu Dance Hall that evening. Huang first went to the dance hall and danced with Li three times. Li, noticing that Huang's actions were strange and unable to bear his harassment, retreated to the restroom to hide. Huang then danced with another dancer, Qiu Lifei, a local. Just as the set was about to end, Jiang arrived. In a hurry, he mistakenly thought that the person dancing with Huang was Li and splashed the acid on Qiu. As a result, Qiu's chest, back, and mouth were corroded. The dance hall staff immediately took Qiu to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to the police, who arrested Huang and Jiang and found a bottle of acid. They were taken to the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer prosecuted Huang and Jiang for inciting and causing bodily harm. The victim, Qiu Lifei, and the Da Hu Dance Hall jointly hired lawyer Wu Peng to represent them and sought compensation for damages. The case has been tried, and yesterday afternoon, presiding judge Xiong Huihua of the Second Criminal Court ordered the two defendants to appear in court. Huang Naiwu was sentenced to ten months' imprisonment for inciting bodily harm, and Jiang Ada was sentenced to ten months' imprisonment for causing bodily harm. The number of days of detention before the verdict is finalized will be counted as two days of imprisonment for each day of detention. The private civil suit will be transferred to the civil court of this court for trial.

Complete Anti-Theft Equipment, Courteous Service

Leaves Shanghai on the Evening of the Fourth, Returns to Shanghai on the Morning of the Seventh

The Puan steamer, operated by the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on the Putuo and Qingdao lines, has a very successful business. Each voyage to Qingdao is fully booked, with ticket revenue exceeding 8,000 yuan per round trip. The anti-theft equipment on the ship is well-equipped, and the first- and second-class cabins and driver's room are completely isolated by radio, and armed escort police are assigned to protect the ship, making it the most completely equipped merchant ship sailing on the coast of our country. Two Brothers Drown in Cold Water Bath 155

Both Around Ten Years Old

Tragedy Caused by Going Out with Neighbor's Children

The day before yesterday afternoon, two boys, around ten years old, went to bathe in the cold water of a small river next to the French Army Drill Ground (i.e., the old site of Xinkang Garden) at No. 1331 Lafayette Road in the French Concession. Due to the deep water and not knowing how to swim, they both drowned in the river. It was not until 6 PM in the evening when a French girl passed by and discovered them that she reported it to the French police station, which notified the fire brigade. People were dispatched to go and fish them out. Clothes were found on the shore, and they were given injections and other rescue measures, but it was already too late. They had already died. An investigation of the surrounding area revealed no family members, so the two bodies were transported by vehicle to the Tongren Fuyuan branch morgue for autopsy. It was not until yesterday morning that family members went to identify the two children. They were Li Zaiming, 12 years old, and Li Zaiqin, 10 years old, brothers, sons of Li Jiren (28 years old, working at the Da Wan Bao), a Suzhou native residing at No. 13, Gaofuli, Saint Mary's Road. They went out to play with the neighbor's children, resulting in this drowning tragedy. The police station reported the incident to Inspector Wang Ren of the Second Special District Court, who went to the morgue to verify that the two children had indeed drowned in the water and ordered the bodies to be handed over to the father for collection.

To Be Managed by the Ministry of Railways

Central News Agency: The inspection team of the Two Railway Administrations recently inspected the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line. Finance Bureau Approves Extension of License Application Period 157

License Applicants Overcrowded, Unable to Handle All Applications

Tobacco and Liquor Industry Petitions for an Extension

Since the tax on tobacco and liquor licenses in this city was taken over by the Municipal Finance Bureau, notices were issued to all industries to apply for registration and obtain licenses in accordance with regulations starting from July 1st. After receiving the order, the tobacco and liquor industries rushed to apply. As the deadline has arrived, the number of people applying for licenses these days has been too crowded to complete the process within the time limit. It is reported that the Finance Bureau has approved the merchants' request and decided to extend the deadline for several days to show consideration. The details are recorded as follows:

Extension Granted 158

The Municipal Finance Bureau reported that the deadline for the tobacco and liquor license tax in this city, which was previously announced, was the end of July. Those who failed to pay taxes after the deadline would be punished in accordance with regulations. The above-mentioned deadline has now expired. In recent days, many merchants in the tobacco and liquor industries have flocked to various tax collection offices to apply for licenses. Each office has received no less than several hundred applications per day. The tax collection offices are handling the license applications as they arrive, but they are somewhat overwhelmed by the sudden influx. Seeing this situation, the Finance Bureau, in order to facilitate the merchants' application for licenses, has decided to extend the deadline for several days to show magnanimity. A report in a certain newspaper yesterday that each tax collection office could only handle twenty applications a day is inaccurate.

Presentation by the Tobacco Exchange Industry 159

The Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Industry Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Bureau of Finance, requesting an extension of the deadline for obtaining licenses to alleviate the difficulties faced by businesses. The original petition stated: "Submitting this petition is to request an extension of the deadline for registration and license acquisition. According to a letter from our association's branch in South Shanghai, over 700 businesses have stated that the Ministry of Finance has transferred the taxation of tobacco and alcohol licenses to the Municipal Bureau of Finance, which began collecting taxes on July 1st. We have also received your association's notice, based on the extended deadline set by the Bureau of Finance, to promptly apply for tax payment and license acquisition in accordance with the law. Upon receiving this, we immediately sent personnel to make payments. However, the windows of the South Shanghai Tax Collection Office are small and located beside the courtyard. Taxpayers have been extremely crowded in recent days under the scorching sun and sweltering heat, which is very difficult to endure. Moreover, the designated office hours are very short, only from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 1:00 PM to 3:00 PM. Currently, many members are traveling long distances by car, waiting for a long time, and still unable to apply for tax payment and registration. They are appealing everywhere, requesting a swift solution to avoid delays and penalties. Therefore, we earnestly request your association to forward this matter to the Bureau of Finance, asking them to consider and alleviate the situation by granting another ten-day extension for registration and license acquisition, and extending the office hours by two hours each in the morning and afternoon to show leniency and facilitate application.” This matter was duly recorded and conveyed. In response, our association believes that the statements made by the South Shanghai branch are indeed factual. Considering the Bureau's short office hours and limited staff, and the large number of members registering within the deadline, the situation is inevitably crowded. Many members may not be able to register even after waiting for a long time. Recently, members have been frequently requesting solutions to avoid delays and to secure proof of registration. With the end-of-July deadline approaching, we are compelled to truthfully petition your bureau to consider the business situation and grant an extension of the deadline for registration and license acquisition for the sake of public convenience."

Lawyer Jin Yu Submits Document to French Consul 163

Requesting Thorough Investigation of Wife and Family's Unjust Arrest

Lawyer Jin Yu, courtesy name Liren, has an office on Ningbo Road in the French Concession and resides at No. 39 Yongyu Lane, Ximen Road. His wife, Mrs. Wang, and others hired rickshaws on the evening of the 27th of last month to go to the Great World amusement center to cool off due to the hot weather. While passing the entrance of the Empire Theater on Avenue Joffre, the rickshaws were stopped by Wang Changshan, an investigator from the Flower Tax Department of the French Concession Police, who suspected them of being prostitutes and took them to the police station, causing trouble. Lawyer Jin has drafted a document and sent it to the French Consul, Mr. Mei, and the Commissioner and Deputy Commissioner of Police, lodging a protest. The document is transcribed below: "Regarding the illegal and abusive arrest and detention of respectable women by Wang Changshan, an investigator from the Flower Tax Department, obstructing their freedom, we hereby report the facts and request a thorough investigation to maintain order. On the night of the 27th of this month, my wife, Mrs. Jin Wang, and others hired rickshaws to go to the rooftop of the Great World amusement center to cool off due to the hot weather. Unexpectedly, a man dressed in black silk clothing, resembling a visitor from another province, suddenly ordered the rickshaws to stop at the corner of Avenue Joffre, in front of the Empire Theater. My wife, seeing that the man was dressed in black, with a white silk belt hanging down a foot or more, and wearing a white straw hat, suspected that he was a rogue blocking the road. Therefore, she was extremely alarmed. Subsequently, the man questioned where they were going, and they immediately replied that they were going to the Great World to cool off. Unexpectedly, the man claimed to be a police investigator and, without asking for details, forcibly ordered them to get out of the rickshaws, intending to arrest them. At that time, my wife still suspected the man's identity and asked to see his police warrant, while stating that she was my wife and showing the Great World's preferential monthly pass to prove her destination. However, the investigator refused to listen and forcibly arrested them, taking them to the Songshan Road Police Station. Later, after the police investigation confirmed that she was my wife, she was released. However, from the time of arrest to the time of release, no less than two hours had passed. According to the law, the body and actions of the people shall not be arrested or detained unless absolutely necessary. Now, my wife and family all reside in Yongyu Lane, at the intersection of Ximen Road and Beile Road, within your concession. In order to travel from south to north, they must pass through Avenue Edward VII and Avenue Pichon. If respectable women are considered prostitutes simply because they pass roads where prostitutes reside, then in the future, your concession should clearly restrict passage on roads where brothels are located, so that women within the concession will know how to avoid them. Currently, your concession has no such restrictions, and the abuse of power and illegal arrests of respectable families by police investigators have occurred repeatedly. Such disturbing actions are not what your concession wants to hear. Moreover, the investigator who arrested my wife and family that night was even more improper: (1) The corner of Avenue Joffre, in front of the Empire Theater, is a major thoroughfare for vehicles. If there is no solicitation along the way, even prostitutes should not be arbitrarily arrested. (2) After my wife repeatedly stated her identity, provided her address, and explained the situation to the investigator, why did the investigator suddenly arrest her without conducting a thorough investigation? (3) The Great World is a legitimate entertainment venue. Why are most of the respectable women arbitrarily arrested by the investigator tourists to the Great World? That night, my wife showed the investigator the Great World's preferential pass. This long pass is not for sale. How could a respectable woman obtain this monthly pass? Therefore, the investigator knew that she was a respectable woman but deliberately arrested her. (4) The investigator abused his power and arbitrarily arrested respectable women. According to the law, he has violated Article 140 and Article 316, Paragraph 1, of the Criminal Law, obstructing freedom, etc."

Weighing 783 Pounds

Currently Performing at Sincere Company

She weighed only five pounds at birth, like a normal person. At the age of twelve, she weighed 85 pounds. At the age of eighteen, she suddenly gained 600 pounds. Now she weighs 783 pounds. Her arms are 26 inches in circumference, her waist is 64 inches, and her legs are 48 inches. She currently eats twice a day, and each meal is less than what a normal person eats. Ministry of Industry Approves Patent for Yu's Chinese Typewriter 166

The Ministry of Industry of the National Government notified Yu Binqi that the Chinese typewriter he invented, specifically the upward-moving printing pins and the horizontal spacing device for interval quantity marking lines, has been examined and approved for a five-year patent. It has been announced and no objections have been raised during the announcement period. A certificate can now be obtained. The structure of the machine is as follows: It has few parts and is made entirely of steel, making it sturdy and durable. For three or four years, the national provinces and cities, such as Sichuan and Yunnan, as well as countries such as England, America, Germany, and France, have been purchasing it, and no repairs have ever been needed. Starting this year, new Song-style copper-steel characters are used, which do not damage after thousands of uses. It can make sixteen copies at once, each clear. It can be used with wax paper and a multi-purpose mimeograph machine produced by the National Goods China Bookstore, making hundreds of copies in less than half an hour. Recently, a long rubber roller has been modified to print long paper at a rate of more than thirty words per minute. All parts of the machine are guaranteed for ten years after purchase, and after ten years it is still worth 100 yuan. Recently, about 400 units have been adopted by the Bank of China, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Yuan Yi Hang, China-American Tobacco Company, Postal Savings Bureau, Postal Supply Bureau, Eurasia Airlines, Sichuan Bank, Sujiaotong Bank, and government agencies, banks, commercial firms at all levels, all of which praise it as a marvel. It is said that the factory is now located at No. 541 Zhaofeng Road, Shanghai. Sample requests and machine tests are welcome.

Red Pill Manufacturing Facility Uncovered on Rue de l'Amiral Bayle 167

Laozha Wang Da and Er are on the run.

Five accomplices are punished separately.

Wang Da and Er specialized in manufacturing poisonous pills. They formerly set up a facility in the Chinese territory of Zhabei. Later, due to the strict opium ban in the interior, they moved their headquarters to the third floor of the Pingsheng Industrial Society at No. 241 Pinghe Lane, Rue de l'Amiral Bayle in the Public Concession at the beginning of this month, and continued manufacturing day and night. However, this place was the main office and did not sell retail. All red pills produced were wholesaled elsewhere by Wang Da and Er. Therefore, the scale was large and the output was abundant. Recently, Zhao Fuhai, a Chinese detective from the Xinzha Police Station, discovered this. He secretly investigated for several days and confirmed the facts. He then reported to the First Special Court and obtained a search warrant. At twelve noon the day before yesterday, he, along with Western Detective Ke Lai, Chinese Detective Yang Peizhang, and Bao Detective Weng Peiyu, Yang Youshan, etc., secretly went to the address to arrest them. Unexpectedly, Wang Da and Er had already fled after hearing the news. Only Yao Wenxin from Changzhou (also known as Yao Panshun), his brother Yao Pansheng, Qiu Yuanxi (also known as Qiu Zhenqing), Wang Ruquan from Yangzhou, and Xie Chengtao from Nanjing, were arrested. Eighteen and a half pounds of red pills, twenty-four pounds of red pill blocks, a small package of morphine, a package of coffee essence, two packages of white powder, six cloth bags, several paper bags, an account book, and all the equipment and wooden boxes for manufacturing red pills were seized and taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court. In addition to detailing the case, the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin prosecuted the defendants according to Article 6 of the Opium Prohibition Law, requesting severe punishment according to the law. When questioned, Yao Wenxin confessed that he rented the house for 20 yuan per month. The bosses were Wang Da and Er, and the five of them manufactured together, but only twice, starting on the eighth of this month. All the red pills were taken away by the bosses to sell. He earned 20 yuan per month, Yao Pansheng earned 10 yuan per month, Wang earned 25 yuan per month, Xie earned 15 yuan per month, and Qiu earned 15 yuan per month. When questioned, Wang Ruquan and the other four all admitted to helping manufacture red pills, but claimed that all wages were received from the boss by Wang Ruquan and distributed. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confession and sentenced Yao Wenxin to two years of imprisonment for manufacturing opium substitutes, with a fine of 1,000 yuan. Wang Ruquan was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes, with a fine of 800 yuan. Yao Pansheng, Xie Chengtao, and Qiu Yuanxi were each sentenced to one year of imprisonment, with a fine of 500 yuan each. Before the judgment is final, the number of days of detention will be offset against the imprisonment at a rate of two days per day, and if the fine cannot be paid, it will be commuted to imprisonment at a rate of three yuan per day. The red pills and equipment seized will be confiscated according to the list.

Cause Originates From Watching a Night Show

Incident Involving Ni Chengji's Fire 169

Wang Jin Attempts to Extort Compensation by Gathering a Crowd

The pavilion room upstairs at the Dong Chunyang divination hall at No. 320 Zhaojiabang Road in the city was subleased to Ni Chengji, who privately set up a mahjong parlor for foreign jadeite. Due to the carelessness of the old chief steward, Da Lang, a fire broke out at 5:30 PM on the 25th of this month, causing the entire house to be burned down and spreading to the adjacent floors. The First District Second Precinct has arrested Ni Chengji and others and sent them to the bureau. After questioning, it was determined that it was an accidental fire, and the burned households were not insured, so they were released with leniency. Ma immediately replied that everyone suffered losses and was not insured, so there was no money to compensate. Unexpectedly, the woman, seeing that her demand for compensation was unsuccessful, invited several hooligans to extort from Ni as Ni was moving the parlor that day, and prevented the Ni family from moving out, led by Wang Jin. The police officer Liu Zhenhai was immediately alerted and detained Wang Jin to the First District Second Precinct for investigation. After questioning by Chief Liu, it was found that the case involved the household that was burned, who attempted to extort compensation unsuccessfully and then resorted to extortion. Summary of Bank Inspection Reports 171

Bank of China The 77th Inspection Report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Preparation Inspection Committee states: "In accordance with the rules, the committee inspected the issuance and branch requisition exchange coupon preparation vault of the Shanghai Bank of China. On July 29, 1934, Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, Wang Yansong, Pei Yunqing, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Wu Weiru, Xu Boming, representatives of the Shanghai Bankers Association, Wang Huailian, Qian Yuansheng, representatives of the Shanghai Money Dealers Association, Li Fusun, Chuan Songnian, representatives of the coupon-collecting banks and firms, Ye Zhuotang, Song Hanzhang, and Zhou Zongliang, representatives of the bank's directors and supervisors, and accountant Wang Zikang jointly held the 77th inspection at the bank. The results of the inspection are listed on the left. The total amount of exchange coupons issued is 11,787,1801 yuan, including 7,972,8264 yuan issued by the bank, 2,103,8542 yuan requisitioned by the branches, and 1,710,0495 yuan requisitioned by the banks and firms. Except for the portion requisitioned by the banks and firms, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection of the branch portion is as follows: The amount issued by the bank and requisitioned by the branches is 10,076,6806 yuan. The amount of exchange coupon preparation of the bank and the branches is 10,076,6806 yuan, including 60,079,6527.42 yuan in cash preparation and 39,970,278.58 yuan in guarantee preparation. The above two items, with the cash preparation accounting for 60% and the guarantee preparation accounting for 40%, were all checked without error. In accordance with Rule 5, this is a formal report. July 29, 1934."

Four Banks The Four Banks Preparation Vault is jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks to specifically handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the vault's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full preparation, with cash preparation accounting for at least 60% and guarantee preparation accounting for at most 40%. It is announced once a week and verified by the auditors and accountants of the Four Banks. The 238th announcement of the Shanghai Preparation Vault on July 28, 1934, is copied below: The amount of banknotes in circulation is 23,435,387 yuan. The total amount of preparation funds is 23,435,387 yuan, including 19,003,187 yuan in cash preparation and 4,332,200 yuan in guarantee preparation.

Establishment of Shanghai Law Bookstore 172

Prominent figures in the legal field, including Zhang Shizhao, He Shizhen, He Shimei, Xu Yuangao, Wang Yintai, Zhang Zhiben, Xu Shiying, Huang Youchang, Chu Fucheng, Shen Junru, Shan Yuhua, Qu Cengze, Wu Guochang, Xu Shihao, Wang Xiaowen, Zong Weigong, Zhou Dingmei, and Ping Jinya, have founded the Shanghai Law Bookstore, with Guo Wei in charge of its affairs. The plan is to write three types of books for each subject: essential meaning, refined meaning, and explanatory meaning. In addition, famous foreign works will be translated, and the laws of various countries will be compared for reference. Thirty to forty manuscripts written by the founders have been printed and are scheduled to be published in September of this year. Furthermore, domestic legal experts have been specially invited to write, such as Dai Xiuzan, Wang Jin, and Tao Xisheng from Beiping, and Weng Jingtang and Ji Huwen from Nanjing. It is expected that this will bring a new perspective to the legal publishing field.

Red Swastika Society Rescues Nantong Woman in Distress 173

The Shanghai General Office of the Southeast Headquarters of the Red Swastika Society received a letter from the Yantai Red Swastika Society stating: "The Yantai Fushan Local Court Procuratorate's letter stated that Hong Zhang has been convicted of abducting Jiang Hongxian. The victim, Jiang Hongxian, is from Nantong, Jiangsu. Although her relatives have been contacted repeatedly, there has been no response. If she is allowed to return on her own, there is a risk of something happening on the way. For humanitarian reasons, please arrange for her to be sent back to her hometown to reunite with her family." She was entrusted to the comprador of a ship to be brought to Shanghai, requesting assistance in sending her back to her hometown. After the woman in distress arrived in Shanghai, the office inquired about her age and origin. She claimed that her name was Zhang Hongxian, from Eighteen Bay, Yudong Town, South District of Nantong, and that her widowed mother was Zhang Wang. She was immediately sent to the Women's Red Swastika Society for temporary care. A letter was immediately sent to the Nantong Red Swastika Society, requesting them to verify if such a person existed. If so, the society was asked to send someone to Shanghai to have Zhang Wang personally claim her. The Nantong branch replied that it had entrusted the Hongxing Shun Tea Shop in Yudong Town to verify that Zhang Wang's daughter, Hongxian, had indeed been abducted last December. The association yesterday sent a special member to accompany Zhang Wang to Shanghai to personally claim her. The Red Swastika Society provided travel expenses and sent her back to Nantong on the Dalian ship. A letter was sent to the Nantong branch, requesting them to notify the local public security bureau or autonomous district office to issue a certificate after receiving the woman in distress, so that the Yantai Fushan Local Court Procuratorate can be informed for investigation.

Jiaozhou Bay Bridge Island Lighthouse Returns to Service 177

Notice from the Hydrographic Office to the Shipping Industry

The lighthouse on Dajiao Island near Jiaozhou Bay on the northeast coast, located at approximately 120 degrees 20 minutes east longitude and 36 degrees north latitude, was temporarily out of service for repairs. It has now returned to service, but its light intensity has been slightly reduced. The light range is 11 nautical miles. Other characteristics remain the same. The local Hydrographic Office issued a notice yesterday to inform the shipping industry to take note.

Reading Q&A 185

Private Life and Ideals (3) 186

Reply to Ms. Xiao Jingjuan and Mr. Luo Fang

A person's private life has a significant determining effect on their thoughts and ideals. Chinese literati have traditionally had a habit of viewing personal private life as a minor matter. This habit has spread widely and has had a great influence. Indeed! Private life, in today's lifestyle based on individualism, belongs to personal private matters and does not require others to interfere.

However, it determines a person's success and failure, advancement and backwardness.

Ms. Xiao, because years of effort have not achieved her ideal, doubts her private life and wants to make a liquidation. This is completely correct. There is a Chinese saying: "A healthy spirit belongs to a healthy body." Without a sound private life, a sound ideal will never be achieved. A person who merely holds a noble ideal is still a fantasy. You have to fight for this goal, and this ideal will truly become your own, and you can turn it into reality. This process is a continuous struggle, including your "public" and "private" life. In your year-round life, in the "public" life, you are subject to social supervision, and it is easy to be discovered if you fall. Conversely, in private life, it is not the case. This aspect of life is your personal matter, and others cannot control it. Even your closest friends can only offer a few words of advice when they discover a certain phenomenon. As for the part you hide, only you know it. Moreover, a person is always a little tolerant of their private life, always thinking that small mistakes are irrelevant. Little do they know that corruption occurs in this fragile part, and its speed of reproduction can sometimes surprise you.

We often see many people's personalities split. We can also see the image of dual personalities in celebrity autobiographies. Especially in an era of transformation, because social contradictions are reflected in personal life, the separation of ideals and life often occurs. Honest, courageous people, they often know their weaknesses and suffer greatly because of them. This has become a theme described in literature. We must not deny it with our eyes closed.

But, is this a strange thing? No! It is not surprising at all. We have briefly mentioned it in "On the Contradictions of Life." Many people die in this contradiction, many people overcome this contradiction, and many people sink. Their victories and failures are not achieved overnight. They all pass through their private lives, morning and evening, either through arduous self-examination or through invisible corrosion, and slowly reach their respective ends.

A person who is sinking into the life of a playboy cannot be a friend of dirty people, nor can he be a warrior to transform society. Conversely, we examine a soldier who deserts on the battlefield, his desertion must be rooted in a lack of clear understanding of the nature of the war, too much leisure in his private life, unable to endure the hardships of battle, and being burdened by his lover, children, and parents, and intoxicated by the enemy's petty gains. All this is the root of his escape. It existed before he went to the front line. As for the occurrence of the act of escape, it is only because of a little fear that his actions are changed. What do we think of a deserter? Simply expressing hatred is useless. If we take the life of a soldier as our ideal life, it is not enough to only have this ideal, and it is also superficial to only hate the behavior of deserters. We must first lower the standard of our private life to a level not far from the life of a soldier. We must study the nature of war, recognize its meaning, and also consider the importance of society and the individual family. We should constantly fight against the life that is not suitable for our "ideal", without letting go of even a single point. We should strengthen the proportion of "knowledge" and the amount of struggle in life, so that we get closer to the ideal day by day.

Naturally, I am not saying that the progress of a person's life is purely—

Depending on one's own intentions, the objective environment determines a person's behavior. But people are by no means mechanical, they can have conscious active functions. A person with ideals should strive to move towards their goals. But he must not ignore his personal private life.

At the same time, we can also examine a person whom we do not yet know deeply from their private life, because what is told here is not concealed at all, and this is the truth. "No heap of garbage is formed without garbage." It is always extremely accidental that pure things are thrown into the trash can. Although the spiritual corruption and depravity of a person have

Although, private life itself is also determined by the social environment. However, in this era of transformation, when the trend of the entire society has been shown so clearly, there are still some people who are caught in a great contradiction between ideals and life. Ideals are often sacrificed due to private life, which is such a pity. Therefore, we dare to say to our readers that a person with an unsound private life is not worthy of pursuing ideals, and he can never be a pioneer for ideals or realize ideals. But this is by no means Confucius's teaching of cultivating oneself first, but a guide to practical life.

The same is true within the scope of reading, drawing inferences from one instance. I will not go into details. Finally, I hope that the two gentlemen, Xiao and Luo, will write to us about their thoughts after reading this reply.

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Military Affairs received a reply telegram from Chairman Chiang, expressing approval for the three-month centralized military training program for students in high schools and above within one year of enrollment, as agreed upon by the two ministries. After receiving the telegram, the two ministries are now formulating military training implementation regulations based on this principle, which will be promulgated by the two ministries in August. Therefore, the academic qualifications of schools at all levels and the curriculum standards for the three types of courses in high school vocational schools and normal schools will inevitably be changed at the same time. The Ministry of Education is now convening consultations with the Ordinary Department, the Higher Education Department, and the Military Affairs Department to reorganize the high school course timetable and vacation dates. Once the military training program is promulgated, the amendments to academic qualifications and high school courses will be announced at the same time.
