Jiangsu Province to Implement Zoned Research on Social Education 206

Dividing the Province into Eight Public Education Zones

Each Zone to Establish a Social Education Sub-regional Research Association

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, in order to improve social education in the province, has specially formulated the "Regulations for the Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Sub-regional Research Association" and promulgated them for implementation. The original text of the regulations is as follows: Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, in order to improve social education in the province, specially divides the province into eight public education zones, each establishing a social education sub-regional research association to study various issues related to social education. Article 2: Each zone's social education research association is organized by the provincial social education institutions, county education bureaus (or county governments in counties where bureaus have been abolished), and county social education institutions within that zone. The articles of association are to be formulated by each zone itself, but must be submitted to the Department of Education for record. Article 3: The names of each zone's social education research association are determined by numbers, called "Jiangsu Province X Zone Social Education Research Association." Article 4: The participating institutions in each zone's social education research association are stipulated as follows: Zone 1: Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Education Center, Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Library, Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Sports Ground, Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Central Public School, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Wujin, Jintan, Jiangdu, Taixing County Education Bureaus, Yizheng, Yangzhong County Governments, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 2: Jiangsu Provincial Jiangning Public Education Center, Jiangsu Provincial National Studies Library, Jiangsu Provincial Nanjing Public Sports Ground, Jurong, Liyang County Education Bureaus, Jiangning, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Lishui, Gaochun County Governments, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 3: Jiangsu Provincial Educational College, Jiangsu Provincial Suzhou Library, Wuxi, Wujiang, Yixing, Jiangyin, Changshu, Kunshan, Taicang County Education Bureaus, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 4: Jiangsu Provincial Yutang Public Education Center, Shanghai, Baoshan, Jiading, Qingpu, Jinshan, Fengxian, Songjiang, Nanhui County Education Bureaus, Chuansha County Government, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 5: Jiangsu Provincial Nantong Public Education Center, Nantong, Rugao, Taixian, Dongtai, Jingjiang, Qidong, Haimen, Chongming County Education Bureaus, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 6: Jiangsu Provincial Qingjiang Public Education Center, Huaian, Siyang, Lianshui, Funing, Yancheng, Xinghua, Baoying, Gaoyou County Education Bureaus, Huaiyin County Government, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 7: Jiangsu Provincial Xuzhou Public Education Center, Tongshan, Peixian, Fengxian County Education Bureaus, Xiaoxian, Suining, Dangshan County Governments, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Zone 8: Jiangsu Provincial Donghai Public Education Center, Donghai, Guanyun, Shuyang, Ganyu, Suqian, Pixian County Governments, County Public Education Centers, Farmers' Education Centers, Public Education Experimental Zone Libraries, Sports Grounds, etc., in each county within this zone. Article 5: The research matters of each zone's social education research association are stipulated as follows: 1. Matters concerning assisting each county in the popularization of social education; 2. Matters concerning promoting the development of social education in each county; 3. Matters concerning social education improvement plans and implementation methods; 4. Matters concerning further education and training of social education personnel; 5. Matters concerning holding discussion meetings and training courses during holidays; 6. Matters concerning social education investigation, statistics, and reporting; 7. Matters concerning publishing social education publications; 8. Matters concerning the investigation of the implementation of social education in each county; 9. Other matters concerning social education research. Article 6: The handling of the affairs of each zone's social education research association adopts an annual system, which is taken in rotation by the provincial social education institutions, education bureaus, or county governments within the zone. Article 7: Each zone's social education research association holds a general meeting once a year. The date is determined by each zone based on local conditions. Each participating research institution must send one representative to attend. Article 8: The location of the first meeting of each zone's social education research association is at the location of the institutions listed first in Article 4, which is convened by the respective institutions. The location of subsequent meetings and the responsible convener are determined by the previous general meeting. The meeting date is limited to two days, which may be extended if necessary. Article 9: For the convenience of research, each zone's social education research association may apply to the Department of Education to suspend the general meeting when necessary. The provincial public education center or education college in each zone may convene the directors and staff of the social education institutions in one or several nearby counties to hold separate meetings to study the special and difficult problems of each county when assisting each county in social education. Article 10: Each zone's social education research association may hold lectures, achievement exhibitions, or other mutual observation activities during the general meeting. The types are determined by the previous general meeting. Article 11: Each zone's social education research association may take a certain issue as the center of research during the general meeting. The central issue is determined by the previous general meeting. Article 12: The provincial public education center or education college in each zone must report on the situation of assisting each county in social education and suggestions for improvement during each general meeting of the social education research association. Article 13: The annual institution of each zone's social education research association shall solicit research questions two months before the meeting and organize and announce them before the meeting. Article 14: In addition to holding meetings for research, each zone's social education research association may also conduct correspondence research. The method is determined by each zone itself. Article 15: The expenses of each zone's social education research association are shared equally by the provincial social education institutions, county education bureaus, or county governments within each zone. The amount for each institution is limited to ten to fifteen yuan per year. Article 16: The person attending from the annual institution serves as the chairman of each zone's social education research association when it is convened. Article 17: At the end of each year or at the end of each meeting, each zone's social education research association must compile the meeting affairs into a report and submit it to the Department of Education for record. Article 18: These regulations are promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education.

Building Libraries and Museums in the City Center 211

Designs Completed, Public Works Bureau Begins Tendering

Literary and Art Hall and Auditorium Also in Preparation

The construction work in Shanghai's cultural district has been actively underway since the issuance of municipal government bonds. The sports ground has already started construction, and the libraries and museums have also begun tendering for construction by the Municipal Public Works Bureau yesterday. It is expected to be completed by the fall of next year. In addition, other cultural construction projects such as the planned public auditorium, literary and art hall, and pagoda are also being prepared separately. A reporter from Shen Shi News Agency specially inquired with the relevant authorities yesterday and obtained the following details:

Completing the Great Shanghai Cultural District 212

According to the provisions of the New Shanghai Plan, the intersection of Sanmin Road and Wuquan Road behind the Municipal Government Building will be designated as the cultural district. The design of the cultural district is cross-shaped. The buildings planned to be built in the cultural district include an auditorium with a capacity of 3,000 people, a library, a museum, a literary and art hall, a court, and an additional 1,000 mu of vacant land reserved for the construction of monuments and other objects. Another 120 mu has been designated in the open space for public gatherings and reviews, as well as other public or semi-public buildings, arranged in a scattered manner. The two sides of the river in the cultural district are being built into a large sports ground and park. The entire project of the above-mentioned cultural district is planned to be completed in the third and fourth phases of the project.

Libraries and Museums to be Built Ahead of Schedule 213

In addition to the sports ground already under construction and the park completed, the Municipal Council decided to build the two major buildings, the library and the museum, ahead of schedule in the second phase of the project, considering the needs of the situation. The establishment of these two museums has a great impact on the education of citizens. Therefore, the Municipal Public Works Bureau has started tendering yesterday. The total cost of each is approximately 300,000 yuan, which will be fully allocated by the Finance Bureau under the municipal government bonds issued this time. All drawings and designs have been reviewed and modified many times. The construction site has been designated behind the Municipal Government Building, and the style is purely ancient palace style.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Announces Tendering 214

The Municipal Public Works Bureau specially announced the tendering for the construction of library and museum projects yesterday. The original text is as follows: "The construction of the Municipal Museum Library project requires inviting merchants to bid for the contract. Any construction factory or construction company that has registered with the Bureau in accordance with the Municipal Construction Factory Registration Regulations and has contracted for projects worth more than 300,000 yuan and has rich experience can go to the Bureau in the city center from now until August 10 to collect the project experience survey form, fill in detailed experience, and submit various supporting documents for review before being notified to collect drawings and bid. Those who are not qualified will have their submitted experience and supporting documents returned."

Preparing to Collect Books and Antiques 215

In addition to the start of the construction of the library and museum buildings, a large number of books and artifacts required inside the two museums still need to be collected over a long period of time. At the same time, in order to enrich and improve the quality and practicality, detailed planning is also required. Therefore, the municipal government plans to immediately organize a book and artifact collection committee to be responsible for handling the matter, so as to formulate rules and regulations separately, solicit them from all prominent aspects, and the municipal government will separately designate regular expenses for continuous purchases. According to another source, the library part is said to be planning to cooperate with the Oriental Library. Since the Oriental Library was destroyed in the "January 28" battle, it has been actively carrying out its restoration, but the location has not yet been determined. Therefore, if it can be realized, it would be a good thing. However, there are still some difficulties in merging in fact. Whether it can be implemented depends on the future facts. As for the museum part, there are also plans to temporarily borrow a part of the Shanghai-stored artifacts from the Forbidden City in Beijing to display in the museum for all circles to visit.

The manuscripts of serial picture books compiled by various bookstores in the city were originally reviewed by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau from January of this year. Now that the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee has been formally established, the Municipal Education Bureau specially notified various bookstores yesterday that the manuscripts should be sent to the Committee for review starting from August 1. After the review and approval, they can be published. The matters of supervision, management, guidance, and improvement are still the responsibility of the Education Bureau.

Since the Shanghai Social Education Society was organized and established by the staff of social education agencies and groups in the city, it has been sparing no effort in carrying out social education work. Spring and Autumn

御香縹緲錄 223

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

However, the large sedan chairs carrying Guangxu and Longyu together occupied a spacious carriage. Yet, not a single eunuch dared to boldly climb up and take advantage of the empty space! The Empress Dowager's imperial carriage was even more extravagant. It was covered by a massive piece of yellow cloth, occupying an entire carriage alone. The remaining space was sufficient for sixty or seventy people to reside in, but who would dare to utilize it? Judging from this situation, being a eunuch in the palace was sometimes not even on par with dogs or horses, and even less than a piece of furniture!

I really couldn't describe the conditions in the row of military vehicles behind us, because I could only see them from afar each time, and never had the opportunity to examine them closely.

In summary, the Empress Dowager's carriage was undoubtedly the most interesting among all these vehicles. At that time, it represented the entire Qing Palace, and the person riding inside was the sole central figure in the Qing Palace, and therefore the central figure of the entire Manchu Empire.

Chapter 12: A Small Court on the Train

The front part of the Empress Dowager's carriage was partitioned into a small boudoir. Although the space was very limited, the style and all the furnishings were created with much thought and effort. Therefore, it was not only beautiful and luxurious, but also in its outline and structure, very similar to the inner chambers of the palace. It was truly a miniature inner palace. However, this only refers to its quality and form. As for the size of the space and the quantity of furniture, the difference was naturally too great - because in this small boudoir, apart from a large bed - the bed was made of redwood, and the Empress Dowager's carriage itself was made of the best teak wood, painted so brightly that it was worthy of her redwood bed - there was not much other furniture that could be considered large pieces. Old-fashioned Chinese beds usually have a frame for hanging mosquito nets, and the Empress Dowager's bed certainly could not be without one. (95)

鴛衾 224

— Yuan Qiao

The aristocratic class truly has many ingenious methods of enjoyment. Just talking about sleep, with spring-cushioned mattresses and wild duck down quilts, it truly fits the humorous interlude in the "Three Smiles" narrative, where Lady Zhou, sleeping in the silk quilt of Wang Laohu's sister, Xiuying, felt as if her body was sliding into a pond. I saw Yuan Yangyu's "New Talks on Mountain Living" saying:

"When I was a child, I heard my late father, the Privy Councillor, say that he once saw in the Song Dynasty palace treasury a brocade quilt of Meng Shu's King. It was wide, the warp thread passed through, the head of the quilt was made into two holes, woven into the shape of cloud plates, covering and buttoning under the neck, like a round collar, with the remaining brocade on both sides, covering the shoulders. This is called a 'Mandarin Duck Quilt.'"

I also had such an ideal, because children often kick off the covers when they sleep alone in bed, especially in spring and autumn when the weather is cool but not cold, making it easier to kick off the covers and catch a chill, which leads to illness. I wanted to specially make a kind of quilt head for them, tied with straps. But I felt it was too troublesome, too restrictive, and inconvenient for getting up quickly. If Meng Chang's Mandarin Duck Quilt was modified a little, it could be made into a most suitable utensil for children.

Originally, a quilt has the meaning of wrapping the body, so wealthy people in Suzhou wear quilts when they die, similar to the meaning of a newborn child being wrapped in swaddling clothes. The same word "quilt" is placed with the word "mandarin duck," and the realm is greatly different. However, the Shu ruler and Lady Huarui did not enjoy it for many years before they were separated, and only obtained the lonely quilt alone. Lady Huarui's warm quilt was taken by others. Mandarin duck dreams are not lasting, and brocade quilts are empty, which is truly excellent material for palace poetry.

牛車棚 225

— Rong Yu

Next to the river harbor stood several embraceable weeping willows. Under the swaying willow branches was a thatched pavilion-like structure, which was the ox-cart shed. In the rural areas of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang regions, wherever rice is grown, this type of ox-cart shed is built almost every five steps, every ten steps, continuously. Not only can the old ox drawing water find shade in the shed, but also travelers walking can rest their feet in the shed if they feel hot; if they encounter rain on the road, they can also take shelter in the shed. Its function is truly almost the same as the "ten-mile long pavilions" of ancient times.

The structure of the shed is very simple, with four crude pillars, and the top covered with a sedge hat-style straw roof. A strong wooden pillar is supported in the shed, passing through a large wooden wheel; the teeth of the wheel are tied to a well sweep; turning the wheel, the well sweep goes up and down; the water in the river harbor then comes up, and is pumped into the fields. The strong and hardy old ox, wearing a blindfold, with a horizontal wood on its back on the wheel, turns and turns, and the water gurgles up. If the ox wants to be lazy and stop, the whip behind it is fiercely lashed. Only when it is exhausted, panting and drooping its tongue, can it see the mature ears of rice in the field, and the corners of the threshing ground full of grain, providing the people in the city with a peaceful life of eating and drinking.

The neat and green rice fields; surrounded by winding river harbors; dotted with sparsely scattered ox-cart sheds, truly rich in painting and poetic meaning. I truly love to watch, and truly love to wander there, and I still constantly miss this beautiful scenery.

But now it is a world of machinery, and the old-fashioned countryside is also following the trend to use water pumps, and the sound of the motor rumbling can be heard in all directions, and the picturesque ox-cart sheds are rarely seen! Some villagers have already slaughtered their plowing oxen, and are no longer happy to plant the fields, so the ox-cart sheds are also eliminated accordingly!

模範婚姻 226

— Ziyun

Mr. Lu went to the park for a stroll and met Ms. Shi. At first, you glanced at me, and I glanced at you. After five minutes, Ms. Shi smiled slightly and swayed her waist as she walked away. Mr. Lu hurried to follow behind. Ms. Shi turned left and right, and Mr. Lu also followed her left and right. Passing by a movie theater, Mr. Lu tentatively said, "Shall we watch a movie?" Ms. Shi turned her head and smiled, stepping up first. Mr. Lu dared not delay, and hurried to buy two tickets, finding seats in the last row. The lights went out, the movie began, and Mr. Lu and Ms. Shi began to ask each other's names, ages, hometowns, education, occupations, and addresses. After the movie was over, they went to a Western restaurant for dinner together. After dinner, Mr. Lu sent Ms. Shi home.

The next day, Mr. Lu wrote a love letter in a scarlet envelope to Ms. Shi, inviting her to meet him at a certain movie theater at nine o'clock the next evening. The next day, Mr. Lu arrived half an hour early, but hurried there and waited for a quarter of an hour. Ms. Shi also came. When the two met, they did not go to see a movie, but went to a snack shop to eat snacks and chat. After eating snacks, Ms. Shi stood up to go home. Mr. Lu said, "There's still time, let's go to a hotel to talk for a while." The elevator of a large hotel carried the pair up to the fifth floor. The waiter led them into a small room, and then there was no more to be said for the night.

Three days later, Mr. Lu and Ms. Shi got married with a simple ceremony. Three days after that, Ms. Shi discovered that Mr. Lu was already a married man, and Mr. Lu also complained that Ms. Shi had too many boyfriends, and both parties agreed to divorce.

This is a modern model marriage.

魚兒也遭殃 227

— Dongzhu

心里哲學的話 228

— (Chengzhao)

The person sitting in the car only looks left and right, fearing that others will see him. However, when turning to the pawnshop, it is the opposite, shrinking his head, fearing that others will see his face blushing.

For a person who has just arrived in the city, it is difficult to find a place to urinate. In fact, if it is written on the wall: "No urination allowed" or there is a large tortoise, then this must be a place where people often urinate.

Usually, when three or more people walk together and chat, there will always be another person who often squeezes back and forth between the two.

Coming out of the bathhouse, if you give a little more "tip", they will be very polite and see you out. Otherwise, perhaps without a word, they will secretly make a face and glare at you.

A handsome male student who is good at talking is most likely to approach female students.

東北四連長 229

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 32: The General Takes Pleasure in Sensual Entertainment All Day Long; Few Soldiers Return While Old and Young Weep

Zhao Weng wiped his eyes twice with a towel, stood up, and comforted him in a very gentle tone: "Don't rush. The newspaper only said that the place was lost and the battalion commander was killed in battle. As for what happened to the four company commanders, we don't know yet. I think that Ziqiang is so loyal and honest, he won't end up in a bad situation." Saying this, his voice choked up again. Guizhi tried hard to hold back her tears, wiped her eyes a few times, and then said to him: "Dad, how do you know about this? Did you specifically buy the newspaper to see?" Weng said: "How would I know? Isn't there a small newspaper subscribed to in the front counter? Today they were discussing it a lot. When they saw me go, they immediately put the newspaper away and didn't mention a word. I saw that their expressions were wrong, and knew that it had something to do with us, so I insisted on getting the newspaper from them to read. I think about it carefully, and things are a bit bad." Saying this, the old man's nose twitched and he cried again. Guizhi handed the newspaper to him, saying: "Take a closer look, I don't recognize the words on it very well." Hearing this, Zhao Weng took the large and small newspapers in his hands again and looked at them one by one. "Aren't they all the same, saying that the national army was defeated and the entire army was annihilated?" Thinking in his heart that the fewer people who knew about this, the fewer people would suffer, and the later they knew, the later they would suffer, so he wouldn't explain it to Guizhi's mother and daughter, which would save himself a lot of trouble in comforting them. So he said to Guizhi: "Based on the newspaper alone, it's also unreliable. Let me go and inquire carefully." Before he finished speaking, Jiang already interjected outside the door, saying: "I've been listening outside for a long time, what should we do about this?" Saying this, he also cried as he came in. Zhao Weng said, "Now we can only find out the news clearly and then think of other solutions. Before we get definite news, we are wasting our efforts by worrying." (446)

Where Travels Lead

揚州法海寺的塔 230

— Yangyang

Yangzhou has been known as a scenic spot since ancient times. In history, geography, and poetry, there are specialized records about it, so Yangzhou is indeed a special place. The ancient Yangzhou, and the Yangzhou of Emperor Yang of Sui, lasted for a long time, so let's not mention them for now. Let's just say that the Yangzhou of the Qianlong era of the Qing Dynasty, which is relatively recent, can be verified in everything; everything is as if it were in front of us. The reason why Yangzhou is able to have a special meaning, and is able to be valued, the biggest reason is nothing more than due to the magnificent buildings and beautiful scenery, this is undoubtedly true. In modern times, someone once suggested that Yangzhou also be included in the scenic area. I remember that the ancient poem said: "In the spring breeze of ten li in Yangzhou road, rolling up the beaded curtains is not as good." It also said: "The spring breeze cuts palace brocade throughout the country, half makes horsecloths and half makes sails." Based on these four fragmented sentences alone, it is enough to represent the beauty and greatness of Yangzhou's scenery!

During the Qianlong dynasty of the Qing Dynasty, the emperor was happy for a while and went to Jiangnan twice. At that time, it was an autocratic regime, it was the world of the Aisin Gioro clan, the people were oppressed under the tyranny of the autocrat, and everything had to be centered on the emperor. However, the scenery of Yangzhou was established, and the famous sites were created and left behind, most of which were due to Qianlong, the so-called "ten li of smoky flowers, nine bends of the abyss;" the so-called "ten li of Sui embankment, the grass is like brocade, one willow tree and one peach tree", all because the people of Yangzhou wanted to flatter Qianlong, and it became the artificial beauty of the smoke and rain pavilions. Unexpectedly, an autocratic emperor who wasted people and money became an expert in setting up scenic areas, and opened the way for future generations of architecture, which is so interesting.

Outside the north gate of Yangzhou, among the small Jinshan Five Pavilion Bridge, there is a temple called "Fahai Temple". Its predecessor was originally called "Lianxing Temple." In the architecture of the Buddhist sect, most of them are full of feudal ideas, which is not surprising. "Fahai Temple" certainly cannot jump out of this range. However, a small temple like Fahai is now even more desolate and dilapidated everywhere, with a thousand kinds of desolation in sight. If the Buddha fruit has a soul, I am afraid it would also be unbearable to look back? Legend has it that when Qianlong visited Yangzhou that year, one day he boated on the Shouxihu Lake, just as "the evening sun and Xiao drums sent several boats home". He happened to turn his head and looked at Fahai Temple in the distance, and suddenly uttered a word inadvertently, saying: "Such a lake, it is a pity that there is one less pagoda. If there is a pagoda, and a cone (that is, a Lama pagoda) is built next to Fahai Temple, then it would be a perfect embellishment."

At that time, the so-called "escort attendants" surrounding Qianlong, in addition to a group of ministers and ministers, there was also a group of local salt merchants who were oppressed on the outside but inwardly flattered. Being fortunate enough to accompany the emperor's chariot was truly glorious for their families and honorable for their ancestors, and there was an unspeakable joy between glances! Having heard the "golden words of the emperor"? They thought he had moved the "莼罏之思". So they immediately quietly started work overnight, combining the blood, sweat, and energy of thousands of sacred laborers, and after a night's work, tomorrow, next to Fahai Temple, there will indeed be an extra pagoda. When Qianlong went to visit the lake again, he had already seen this large radish-style cone next to the temple. He just laughed it off, asking why it was built so quickly? Those salt merchants shouted "Long live" three times, and replied in unison: "The Holy Emperor is protected by a hundred spirits", but they had long forgotten how many blood, sweat, and energy had been sacrificed last night, and even cost the lives of some people.

Now things have changed, the people who built the tower and the people who watched the tower have both turned to dust, leaving only this hastily built tower, just for later generations to mourn!

Free Talk - Long Live the Public Language Wu Zhihui

—A Letter in Response to Cao Juren's Discussion on the Public Language Problem—

Mr. Cao: It has been a long time since I have had the pleasure of learning from you. However, I often read your works in many publications, and I have benefited a lot.

Regarding the issue of classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese, and the public language, I also wanted to join in the excitement and add a few words. However, in recent years, I have been studying the seventeen histories. Where should I start? Ni Yunlin said, "Speaking is vulgar," because he was afraid of becoming vulgar himself and did not want to speak. I know that I cannot produce ivory from my mouth and that everything I say will be vulgar, so I dare not speak. Therefore, even when faced with such a lively issue, I still dared not say anything. Thank you for mentioning my science and engineering issues in relation to this question. I have not yet fulfilled your kindness by saying a few words. It is because I learned from you in the past that I hope others will engage in science and engineering, but I myself am neither scientific nor engineering. This is truly to the point. Since then, I have found it annoying to be constantly poked, and I have had nothing to say. Now that you have asked me about the issue of classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese, and the public language, I will write down what I want to say in my heart for you to laugh at.

To sum up, I will first say one sentence: it is indeed difficult for classical Chinese to die out completely in a short period of time. But to say that it will revive and replace vernacular Chinese is a joke. And it is as certain as the iron tree cannot bloom. Mr. Wang, Mr. Liu, and others suddenly advocated that middle schools should focus on classical Chinese after junior high school, with seven parts of intention to save people, and perhaps three parts of intention to defend the way. Because they saw that the examination papers and the graduates were really bad at classical Chinese and not suitable for the official style, which made it difficult for them to find a job. They wanted to save these "job-finding gentlemen," so they hoped that the schools would open the door of convenience and give them the tools to find a job. This seven parts is compassion. I think Mr. Wang and Mr. Liu are unbiased and are sacrificing for others, not protecting themselves. As for the three parts of defending the way, it is a matter of opinion. They occasionally feel that classical Chinese can help preserve the way they hope for a little more. Just as vernacular Chinese or public language advocates also believe that they can be superstitious about the relationship between the body of writing and the way. Moreover, with only three parts, Mr. Wang and Mr. Liu can also be forgiven.

However, I do not believe that the style of writing is related to defending the way. If there is a way in classical Chinese, why did the Three Principles of the People of the Premier write in vernacular Chinese? If vernacular Chinese is entirely the way, why do vernacular Chinese writers often hear criticism of certain schools and certain novels? It can be seen that classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese, and the public language are only tools. There is only a difference between being easy to popularize and not easy to popularize. In our current situation, if we rationally allocate, that is, in terms of schools, only 50% can enter the officialdom, 15% can teach in schools, and 80% are expected to write about agriculture, industry, and commerce. In middle school, all 100% should focus on their science, chemistry, mathematics, and should also learn science and engineering, and must also learn foreign languages. Then, it is enough for them to be able to read Premier's Three Principles of the People in easy vernacular Chinese. In high school, the 20% who are divided out should also learn some classical Chinese that is suitable for the official style. In colleges and universities, they should then go to study law, politics, literature, and philosophy according to their interests. The number is also sufficient for the Examination Yuan to select and the government agencies to employ. I am still afraid that there are too few roads and too many people who want to go out. Why must we focus on the official style in junior high school and imply where the way out is, but in fact, this road does not work, and the society is left with a large number of middle-level hooligans? Therefore, Mr. Wang and Mr. Liu are trying to save people, but they are actually harming people. Mr. Wang has never entered the animal realm, but Mr. Liu is like me, who has entered the animal realm. Looking back, which child was not forced to read the Four Books and Five Classics? Of course, no one dared to question classical Chinese. However, how many of the one or two dozen scholars selected in each county were fluent? Mr. Zhuang Sijian often said: "The articles in the examination are for seeing officials, not for seeing friends." Compared with the current middle school students, the minority are no less than the children of the past. Those who are outstanding, such as Mr. Liu, were also the smallest minority at that time. Therefore, it is not that only classical Chinese can produce talents! In the end, classical Chinese can become literature, vernacular Chinese can also become literature, and the public language will certainly become literature. However, classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese, and the public language have different levels of ease of popularization. Of course, vernacular Chinese is easier to popularize than classical Chinese, and the public language must be easier to popularize than vernacular Chinese. If it comes to literature, I am afraid that classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese, and the public language are all only for the minority. In fact, even the official style and the like only require classical Chinese, but not classical Chinese literature. Even those who write vernacular Chinese well may not be able to write that official-style classical Chinese. It is a pity that as soon as they write classical Chinese, they immediately hope that they will understand literature. Therefore, the incoherence of classical Chinese arises from this.

In this war between classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese, there are many admirable works. I have paid attention to two articles. One is Mr. You Mojun's "Talking about the Public Language from the Perspective of Middle School Students' Writing." He cited the Zhejiang joint entrance examination, with the title "The Friend I Admire Most." One of them is in classical Chinese, saying, "Since ancient times, heroes and great men..." which does have a hint of Guwen Guanzhi. But Mr. You wants to ask what use it is in daily life? I replied: "Only call it literature. I am afraid that if you ask this gentleman to handle official documents, he may not be able to be very clear." Therefore, do not only blame classical Chinese. In this joint entrance examination, Mr. You also cited a vernacular Chinese piece, saying, "The friendship of ancient gentlemen is as light as water..." Mr. You also criticized it as indigestible vernacular Chinese. However, the reason for digestion or indigestion is also because it is being done as literature. Everyone now wants to build a public language and overthrow vernacular Chinese. I am afraid that it is vernacular Chinese literature that has caused the trouble. Therefore, Mr. Hu Shi resists classical Chinese and tells people to work hard in vernacular Chinese literature. I do not know that on the other hand, vernacular Chinese literature is not competitive. Only a few can do it well, just like classical Chinese literature, which is ultimately for the minority. Unconsciously, people also vernacular Chinese literature, ghosts also vernacular Chinese literature, just like Guwen Guanzhi often collapsed on the stage of classical Chinese. And the public language unceremoniously came to denounce and punish it. Because in terms of tools, vernacular Chinese is naturally superior to classical Chinese because it is easy to popularize. However, once it comes to literature, it is smoky and chaotic. Good classical Chinese literature, such as Yuan Zhonglang's essays, is only for people in ivory towers to relieve boredom, and good vernacular Chinese literature is only for friends in the pavilion to relieve boredom. Most of the monsters are simply inexplicable to the public, just like Guwen Guanzhi. Therefore, here, I would like to contribute: Do not build a public language and then follow it with public language literature. If you can build a public language literature, of course, it is like Mr. Hu Shi who built vernacular Chinese literature into vernacular Chinese. But in the end, there will be an overthrow.

The other of the two articles that I paid attention to this time is Mr. Tao Zhixing's "The Road to the Public Language Movement." He said: Public language and public writing (writing is writing, not literature. Classical Chinese, classical Chinese writing, classical Chinese literature; vernacular Chinese, vernacular Chinese writing, vernacular Chinese literature: public language, public language writing, public language literature, that is, the public language will need literature in the future, let the public create it themselves, do not be like vernacular Chinese literature, which is still a few classical Chinese literati who changed their heads and faces to handle it.) must be united. United in degree, united in need, and united in consciousness. He advocates a three-pronged approach to symbols. Chinese characters must be taught, phonetic alphabets must be taught, and using phonetic alphabets to spell out the public language must be taught even more. I think his meaning is also to promote vulgar writing and simplified Chinese characters. That is, sometimes when caught off guard, adding a few homophones is also allowed by his teacher. I also allow him to combine Chinese characters, phonetic symbols, and homophones when they are not enough to use. When public education is popularized, let the able people in the public sort out a clue; when the San You in the hutong need hutong leisure products, let them create public literature; do not let today's literati and scholars turn blue in the face, set writing examples, and create vocabulary, as if the public should come to receive our decrees. Seeing homophones and phonetic symbols mixed in, they are strictly forbidden. If this is the case, it is also affected by traditional thinking, and what is the difference between the classical Chinese gentlemen who say "it existed in ancient times, it has been passed down"? Classical Chinese existed in ancient times, which is ridiculous. Vernacular Chinese gentlemen say that it exists in the West, and they must introduce it to the public as soon as they learn and practice it. This is the incurable stain that vernacular Chinese will be revolutionized by the public language. Literary genius is very rare, and Dong Shi imitates it, there is a fixed format, plus shackles. Therefore, we must be very careful about advocating literature in the public language. It is best to follow Mr. Tao's meaning and let the public create it themselves, instead of handling it on their behalf.

Moreover, according to my guess, Mr. Chen Wangdao and others put out this banner of public language. The public is vertical, speaking to the majority of classes. Although there is also the intention to slowly connect to the horizontal aspect, one person's speaking can make 400 million people understand together, but according to my nonsense, I am afraid that Mr. Chen's intention was not to jump to that in one leap. What 400 million people understand together is called a unified language, not the public language that is urgently needed in the first step. You have the public, and we have the public. Your public combines your language and writing. Our public combines our language and writing. Your public and our public have a unified language and writing, and then they combine with each other. A kind of unified language, which is still created by the public, is the second step. This is probably not a utopia. You and we often talk to each other now. You are not you, and we are not we. There is its own incorrect mixed official language. The mixed official language must be the unified language of the future. It may be quite appropriate to bring a little bit of Beijing dialect, but it must really meet Mr. Tao's standard of "the best to listen to and willing to learn." However, even British English and American English cannot conform to the single style of Yorkshire. A single style is the opposite of an imperial decree. The concept of a single style in our country has not only entered the political world, biting tightly on the dick, and the chicken legs cannot be pulled away, but also in the literary world, moving a hair will cause a sad feeling of losing a parent. The crime of destroying unity is the greatest crime in the political world. Is it not the same in the academic world? Well, I admire literature, and I admire both classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese literature. It is a pity that I have no strength to look at people, and I am only putting on small feet, which is really disgusting, and therefore harmful to your country and your family. Therefore, I dare to make a conclusion to answer your clear question:

Literature does not die, disaster does not stop.

Well, long live the public language! If the public language and writing are united, write some simple science and technology articles to benefit the public's rice bowl, which would be especially perfect. Otherwise, how much is knowledge worth a catty? It cannot be eaten when hungry, and it cannot be worn when cold. Instilling everyone with knowledge to cry with their heads in their arms, crying so that the public is skinny, and it will not be easy to carry out any revolution or resist the enemy! Thinking back to the previous days, you are not good, overthrow you, I will do it, you come I come, it is still the same thing. Where is the fundamental weakness? It is that you yourself are neither scientific nor engineering. I cannot help but feel ashamed of you, sir. Well, I wish you good health!

Your younger brother Jingheng bows on the 29th

Also: Yama has not endowed me with literary talent. I am a "fart fart, really unreasonable" public, and I hope you will forgive some missing words and errors. The society is really dizzy now. Mr. Liu Bannong is a great expert in phonetic literacy, but he is pulled to be counted as a literary man, which is considered respect for him. I do not know that it is scolding him, it is burying him, and it is so upside down. You must laugh at it too.

Gejiu Factory Li Qiao

—Mine Communications II—

"When you get to the factory, you can't be like you were at home. You have to remember: You have to endure everything - for example, for example -"

Before I went to the factory, the acquaintance who "walked the water" (1) told me everything about the factory and told me what I should pay attention to. He was very concerned about me and hoped that I could find a woman's money in the factory so that I could go home and marry a wife! But I never knew that life at the factory would be so bad!

Everyone here is busy working all day long. In the morning, before it is light, a cook with a grass rope tied around his waist and a black turban soaked in sweat on his head has already cooked the rice and is just waiting for people to eat. Rubbing his eyes, which were smoked by the firewood smoke, he shouted loudly to the people sleeping in the kitchen:

"Get up! Get up!..."

The shout was only three times, and the cook felt that he had fulfilled his obligations and stopped caring. If there were still people sleeping soundly at this time because they were too tired, the boss would walk out of the "noble room" (2) unceremoniously, pick up a bucket full of water without saying a word, and pour it down on their heads! This would startle you from your dream as if you had been struck by lightning, and you would run to the dark sky all wet.

Squatting on the ground around a stinky kerosene lamp, just as you hear the crisp first crow of the rooster announcing the dawn, people are eating in a mess.

What is there to eat besides that only bowl of "Old Mother Soup" (3) every day? But it is more precious than ginseng soup! People who wash their faces in the morning are not qualified to eat it. This high rule is called "no soup with a washed face, no face washing with soup." Because the water in this place is only relied on when it rains in May and June to dig a square mud pond and store it to survive. When it is dry, the water is sold for one or two yuan per load, and sometimes you cannot even buy it. Therefore, even a pond of unbearably dirty and smelly water, with feces and urine, will be casually stirred with a little alum and used as drinking water.

But as a result, plague, scabies... and other diseases breed playfully in the crowd. Death, terrible death, also comes unceremoniously!

But what is so great about death? In this place, the death of a person is like the death of an ant being trampled. As soon as a miner gets sick, not only is there no medicine, but the boss also mercilessly forbids him to sleep in the kitchen. Therefore, they have to sleep in the open outside the kitchen, but what kind of situation is it outside the kitchen? The strong wind blows and howls day and night, and the mournful sound of hungry wolves comes from near and far at night, making people feel very terrified. In this situation, even if they are not taken away by hungry wolves, their lives will end quickly!

After death, the body is thrown far away in a cave or a desolate and uninhabited valley.

Such death and abandonment do not receive pity or compassion in this place. The hearts of the living are only focused on work, picking and digging all day long, as if they want to shovel away these bare mountains, so busy that they cannot even catch their breath!

Sometimes, when you want to stretch your back and take a breath of leisure, a stern voice will be thrown into your ears:

"You motherfucker, if you can't do it, get out! This place is not a..."

Get out, can he really easily let you get out? If you cannot stand this scolding or this hard work, and you sneak away, he will send someone to look for you, saying that you have run away with something of his (or that you have run away with "monthly living money" (4)), and he will cruelly hang you up and beat you! Until you are about to die, a heavy pair of shackles will be put on your feet. From then on, you will always faithfully work for him without pay!

Because this is the factory rule here, the government will not care about you!

Such things terrified my little heart when I first went there! I, a young "next class" (5) kid, was always working with a cold sweat.

...I was always awkward and afraid in all my actions. My heavy heart was always thinking of my parents who were far away!

On the fifth day after I arrived at the factory, the "walking water" acquaintance was leaving me to go home. I looked at him with attachment, as if I would be eaten by the boss as soon as I left him. I almost wanted to cry as I looked at him!

But I didn't dare!

(Notes) (1) Walking water refers to people from other places who come there to do business. (2) The boss's room is called the noble room. (3) Old Mother Soup is a small bowl of soybeans, ground finely, and boiled into a clear soup for forty or fifty people to eat. (4) Monthly living money refers to wages. (5) Next class means going down into the cave to carry ore.

(Note) "Mine Communications I" was published on June 15 and 16 in Free Talk. It has been a month since Mr. Li Qiao sent the continuation from Yunnan from far away.

I From the East (12) Hoshino

At midnight, I came out of the Hawaiian village. The driver found a coconut outside the village and gave it to me as a souvenir. He also took me to see the Chinese residential area. It is said that the Chinese influence here has been gradually taken away by the Japanese. We returned to the ship, opened the coconut, and there was only a little milky juice inside. The coconut meat is white and tastes a bit like fresh lotus root and chestnut.

In the Pacific Boat

The Pacific shipping industry is now controlled by the British, American, and Japanese. The Japanese are represented by the Nippon Yusen Kaisha; this company can be said to be a part of the Japanese Navy. The ship prices are very cheap, and the tonnage is relatively small. The Americans are represented by the American Mail Line and the Dollar Steamship Company. The old Dollar was originally a Canadian and was known as the "Old Man of the Pacific." Now he is dead! His company's business is progressing very quickly. In recent years, they have built two very large trans-Pacific liners; one is the President Hoover and the other is the President Coolidge. It is said that the contents of these two ships can be compared with the largest liner in the Pacific, the Empress of Japan. The British side is represented by the China Navigation Company. The capital of this company is controlled by the British, American, and Canadian. It not only does business in the Pacific, but also controls the route from London to Canada. The Canadian Pacific Railway (CPR), a lifeline of Canada from the Atlantic to the Pacific, is the main body of this company. Although the China Navigation Company only has four ships in the Pacific, the exquisiteness of the ships is most praised by tourists. The two smaller Empress of Asia and Empress of Russia sail between Vancouver and Tokyo, Shanghai, and other ports. As for the larger Empress of Japan and Empress of Canada, they travel from Vancouver via Hawaii to various ports in the Far East. The Empress of Japan has a displacement of 40,000 tons and is the largest and fastest ship in the Pacific. I only spent seventeen and a half days on this ship from Canada to Shanghai this time.

Life on a Pacific ship is very interesting for those who are not afraid of wind and waves. In this 40,000-ton floating city, you can enjoy all the material life of modern civilized people: libraries, cinemas, dance halls, ballrooms, swimming pools, smoking rooms, entertainment rooms, barbershops, laundries, hotels, dining rooms, grocery stores, etc., are all cleverly arranged on the ship. Elevators go up and down, making people forget that they are at sea. Moreover, life on the ship is sometimes better than in modern big cities. The guests on the ship are not in a hurry, and the passengers meet, talk, smoke, play cards, and eat together every day, which naturally creates a close relationship. Moreover, everyone has no other purpose, and there is no material or interest separation between people, so the air on the ship is not found in modern large hotels or summer resorts.

Due to the decline of international trade, most of the cargo holds and cabins on trans-Pacific mail ships are empty. My fellow passengers this time were especially few, and the number of sailors was several times more than the number of passengers. Except for senior crew members, the sailors on the China Navigation Company's ships are all Cantonese. Among the passengers, there are yellow and white people. There is only one Chinese in first class, and he is also a shareholder of the China Navigation Company. There are more Chinese in second class. In third class, except for five or six Filipinos and Americans, the rest are all Chinese.

Page 21

Special Telecommunications Publication The Voice of the Telecom Industry Promoting Telecommunications to Rural Areas Li Bing

We see the prosperity of cities, the completeness of all communication facilities, and the convenience of social use in all aspects. However, because telecommunications bureaus are not yet widespread in the interior, there are people who want to send telegrams but have no way to send them, and want to make phone calls but have no way to connect. Therefore, those who live in remote inland areas have fewer opportunities to use telecommunications than those who live in cities. If the telecommunications industry only relies on connecting large cities or important towns, then the rapid transmission of information is only a benefit enjoyed by a few people. The effectiveness of telecommunications has not been maximized, and the use of telecommunications has not been broadened. In terms of benefiting the public, it is not perfect. Therefore, urban telecommunications are important, but rural telecommunications should also be developed. Therefore, promoting telecommunications to rural areas is a point that the authorities should pay attention to.

Promoting telecommunications to rural areas is not difficult to believe, but it is difficult to implement. Expanding long-distance lines and expanding a large number of bureaus is limited by financial resources and cannot be done overnight. Therefore, the next level of remedial measures is no more than two ways:

(A) On the basis of existing trunk and branch lines, expand them separately to connect cities, towns, and villages for the purpose of connecting reports and phone calls.

(B) In places where no report and phone bureaus are established, post offices will deliver telegrams free of charge.

The former is the report and phone business agency that the Ministry of Communications expanded this year, and the latter is what is called "postal telegram transfer". With the agency for report and phone business, the nearby people can all have access to reporting and phone calls. With the implementation of postal telegram transfer, where the post office can reach, the telegram can also reach, which is both economical and convenient.

However, the above-mentioned methods are only a kind of remedy, and the Ministry of Communications has never limited itself to this. Once the effectiveness is obvious and the business is developed, the original report and phone agency can be transformed into a new bureau, and the places that currently need postal telegram transfer will also be reduced due to the expansion of telecommunications. In short, we will observe the development of the telecommunications business and determine a plan for continuous improvement. The date of realization is not far away.

In the past, those in charge of telecommunications administration only focused on short-term interests and lacked long-term plans. Their attention was focused on prosperous and important cities. Occasionally, the business community in the interior would request the expansion of lines, but they would often be met with many difficulties. Now, although the measures taken in the north cannot be said to be thorough, they are enough to show the authorities' intentions, and they have already implemented the method of "promoting telecommunications to rural areas."

Metered Telephone Fees Kuang

The previous issue of this publication contained a discussion on public telephones. Telephones in various parts of our country are charged on a monthly basis and not based on the number of calls made. Therefore, busy users call frequently every day, while idle users regard the telephone as a decorative item and are happy to lend it to others. In fact, the telephone bills paid are the same. The more calls made, the lower the price. Ideally, some people who want to make phone calls but think that installing a telephone is uneconomical often ask their neighbors for help to make phone calls. This is actually a loss to the telephone bureau. Telegrams are charged by the number of words, and electric lights are charged by the number of degrees. Both are public utilities, but only telephones are not. Is this not unfair? In Europe and the United States, the number of telephone calls is used as the standard for paying fees. There are many examples of this being implemented to this day. Please allow me to explain it so that people can learn from it.

(A) Telephone Call Counter - Since telephone calls are charged by the number of calls, the recording of the number of calls is very important. If the driver personnel have to record each user's call each time, it will inevitably make the job busier and affect the connection (this refers to common-battery or magneto telephones). Therefore, a telephone call counter is specially installed in the telephone bureau. The form is quite exquisite and compact, like an electric meter. There are numbers on it that can rotate. As long as the current passes once, the unit of the number will also rotate once. Therefore, if a user calls and connects, the counter of that user will record it once, without any error. At the end of the month, the total number of calls can be viewed and a bill can be sent to the user to collect fees. According to this method, fees are paid for each call, which can avoid users making unlimited calls and can also eliminate the borrowing of telephones.

(B) Fee-Paying Telephone Device - There is also a kind that is widely used in long-distance telephones in the United States, which is called "fee-paying telephone". This method is used for long-distance telephones, and the fee for each call varies depending on the distance of the circuit. The American currency system has five cents, ten cents, and twenty-five cents. The telephone fee is also based on these three kinds of currency. For example, if A needs to call B, after the telephone is picked up and the driver personnel answers, they will instruct A to put the fee (five cents or ten cents or twenty-five cents) into the slot on the telephone. When the money falls and touches the mechanism, the driver personnel can hear the sound and can also know if it is a mistaken投. After knowing that there is no error, the connection can be made immediately. Also, if the user called is unable to talk due to a problem, the mechanism of the telephone bureau will automatically release the fee that was paid from the return slot below the telephone so that it can be returned to the original owner, without having to waste it.

The above is only a general description of the situation, but it can also be seen that overseas countries have also given much consideration to the problem of charging telephone calls by the number of calls. Therefore, there have been various inventions. In recent years, automatic telephones in our country have become more and more developed, and long-distance telephones have also been expanded a lot. Applying mechanical equipment to charge by the number of calls seems to be limited by economic conditions and cannot be done. Then, adding public telephones in public places and having the agents charge by the number of calls to facilitate the citizens and increase revenue may not be a way to remedy the situation.

Explanation of the New Regulations on Telegraph Savings for Fee Reporter

Since the Ministry of Communications promulgated the new regulations on telegraph savings, it has tried its best to implement telegraph price reductions within the possible scope, which has been convenient for all walks of life. However, the various new regulations on savings that have been promulgated may not be fully understood by people in society and still need to be vigorously publicized. Now, we have investigated several points raised in a letter from Zhang Yibo, manager of the Wudi Brand Zhenjiang Factory Co., Ltd., to the Telegraph Administration Department. After the Telegraph Administration Department gave a detailed explanation, we will now record the (Mr. Zhang's) questions and (the Telegraph Administration Department's) answers as follows:

(Question 1) When sending a telegram to a place with a registered telegraph address, adding the name of the addressee requires counting six characters.

Example 1 1681 Wuxi Tan Gongchen

According to the above example, six characters must be counted. It is more economical to use the telephone instead.

Example 2 Telephone 671 Wuxi Tan Gongchen

In the above example, it can be counted as four characters. According to this method of calculating fees, using a registered telegraph address requires adding the name of the addressee, which costs two extra characters. It is better not to use a registered telegraph address and use the telephone instead, which can save money.

(Answer) Article 1 of the Regulations on Registered Telegraph Addresses states: "The addressee of a telegram may choose one character to replace the name and address of the person." Therefore, according to the regulations, the registered telegraph address already includes the name of the addressee. If the name of the addressee is added after the registered telegraph address, it will become redundant. Furthermore, the method of registered telegraph addresses is to provide convenience for merchants who send and receive a lot of telegrams, while the method of replacing the addressee's address with a telephone number is to provide convenience for private households that do not send many telegrams. The two are not mutually exclusive.

(Question 2) When a telegram is sent to a place where the local telephone is divided into several districts.

Example 3 Concession Telephone 94013 Shanghai Tu Xiaochao

The right requires counting five characters. It is better not to use the telephone and use a detailed address.

Example 4 No. 2, Jianye Lane, Shipipi Lane, Nanshi, Shanghai Tu Xiaochao

It is also counted as five characters. According to the above example, using the telephone does not save money compared to using a detailed address for the telegraph fee. However, when the message is transmitted by the machine, the code used to transmit the telephone instead of the name and address is less. The more or less we pay is proportional to the amount of code that is transmitted. Now it is not so. The amount of code transmitted is the same for less and more, which is difficult to understand. Moreover, the original purpose of using the telephone to replace the name and address was to save trouble and money. Since it does not save money, what is the value of this method?

(Answer) According to your letter:

"Concession Telephone 94013 Shanghai Tu Xiaochao" needs to be counted as five characters, which is still the method recorded in the old regulations. According to Articles 4 and 9 of the New Regulations on Telegraph Savings, it should be written as:

"Shanghai Telephone Concession 94013 Tu Xiaochao" is only charged as four characters.

New York Stock Market Trading Quiet 238

According to a report from New China Trading Company, the New York stock market yesterday (the 30th) saw quiet trading and weak prices. Transactions of mailed stocks were particularly sluggish due to the drought and impending disaster, which is bound to reduce the purchasing power of farmers in the Midwest. However, the market gradually rebounded at the close. Various shares on the small exchange were also slightly lower than before. The bond market was mixed, with US government bonds up slightly. Foreign bonds showed mixed ups and downs, and German bonds fell slightly. Commodities, including mixed grains, rose due to the drought and inevitable poor harvest. The total volume for the day was 810,000 shares. (Securities) After initial weakness in specific stocks in the morning, the market recovered well. If the news remains favorable, prices should continue to rise. (Mixed grains) After initial declines in wheat in the morning, buying interest intensified and prices soared. According to preliminary private reports, the wheat harvest is estimated at 475 million bushels and corn at 161.6 million bushels. Losses of corn in the fields continue. In general, it is advisable to buy when prices fall. (Cotton) The market rose due to private estimates favoring long positions. Current cotton export demand is poor, and cloth sales are also sluggish, but the foundation is solid. Cotton mills have reduced production by 25%, with the possibility of further reductions. The New York Cotton Exchange estimates total consumption at 13,564,000 bales and inventory at 10,083,600 bales. (Rubber) The market generally rose due to purchases from US manufacturers. According to estimates from Singapore, traders are still stockpiling, and the amount on the market has decreased by 11,000 tons compared to last month, indicating a strong technical position. The Dow Jones index is listed on the left.

Yarn and Cotton: US Cotton Rise Suddenly Discovered 239

Yarn and cotton float urgently to cover positions.

The yarn market is trending firm, and a rising trend is emerging. US cotton is rebounding, and current yarn demand in North China is strong. Tianjin merchants continue to procure, so the sentiment is bullish, and buying interest is stronger. Floating positions are particularly urgent to cover. However, Japanese traders' short positions remain calm. The future depends on actual sales for advances and retreats.

August Standard Cotton Levy Special Certificate 245

The Shanghai Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange will levy a special deposit of 3 yuan in cash per dan for new August standard cotton transactions made from August 1st this year. Both deposit accounts will be charged one side, which has been announced in the market.

Grain: Monthly Powder and Wheat Delivery Volume Average 247

The powder futures are being delivered without a market. The total number of delivery warehouse receipts is only 37,000 bags of returned goods from the Bund. Because most of the warehouse receipts have been directly offset in advance, the actual appetite of the trades has been satisfied. For this month's warehouse receipts, they have mostly been withdrawn for cash and loaded at any time. Therefore, before delivery, cash has been gradually withdrawn and loaded, and a part has been recovered by shorts. Therefore, only these returned goods from the Bund remain at the end of the month. This batch of warehouse receipts is withdrawn and loaded by Beiyang trades such as Yingkou, Qinhuangdao, and Yantai for actual sales.

The wheat futures market is closed due to the month-end settlement, and there are not many spot deliveries at the end of the month, because they have already been directly reported and offset. A total of 18 cars are currently delivered, which were released on the 27th, etc., and the receivers are the 28th, etc. They are probably distributed by the factory. In addition, there are also 30-40 cars that are directly offset. Foreign wheat has risen by another 3-5 jiao. Spot wheat is bullish due to the rise in foreign wheat, and the factory appetite is particularly greedy. Yesterday, it rose by another 4-5 fen. A total of 16,000 bags were opened throughout the day, which were received by Fu Xin, etc. High-grade wheat is 3.55-3.5 yuan, and medium and secondary grades are 3.45-3.17 yuan.

Dongxin Japonica rice in the north of Shanghai has fallen by half a yuan 248

(South of Shanghai) Yesterday, there were slightly more sources from various trades, estimated to be 17-18, (about nearly 3,000 shi) while the sales in the market were still average. Therefore, there were some sellers who shouted high prices, and some who shouted fixed prices, so the situation was uncertain. However, by the close of the market, the overall situation was still calm. For example, Japonica rice and green-cornered Songsi and other late rice from Chang Trade, Su Trade, and South Harbor, etc., had no ups and downs, while Du Yangjian had no honor or disgrace, and Yin changed, and there was no market for Yuan goods. Pudong new Japonica rice still opened at 12 yuan.

(North of Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of the river was 11-12, and the sales in the market moved slightly. The market price of white japonica rice increased by about 1 jiao, the thin rice, Yang Du Bu Jian stabilized, and the customer tip price increased by nearly a jiao. The source of Dongxin Japonica rice was quite prosperous, estimated to be more than 400 shi, but retail sales were flat, resulting in a price drop of half a yuan.

After Saigon Rice Arrives in Shanghai

Foreign Rice Rise Suddenly Killed 249

Yesterday, the market for foreign Ke Xian rice, initially due to inland greedy purchases, the sentiment and the market continued to rise, and the arrival was not prosperous, and the inventory at the bottom was getting thinner every day, the market atmosphere was quite tense. After the opening price, the high-grade and each grade rose uniformly, especially Xiang Xian and brown rice were popular. Xiang rice opened 1,720 bags of Ji Jing and Jing Ji oil brown rice, Wuxian 700 bags, Shashi Ji Xian 230 bags, Chuzhou Ji Xian 1,000 bags, Shashi Hankou and other brown rice 3,500 bags, totaling 8,150 bags. Except for more than 100 bags in this street, all were purchased by the mainland, and the price was a large corner higher than the previous market. There is not much foreign rice in the market, and it is still continuing to be bullish. However, yesterday, the French company’s ship Yan Lu shipped 19,500 bags of No. 1 round-grain Saigon. This batch was loaded by the experts themselves in Shanghai, and after adding donations and taxes, the cost was 45 jiao higher than in Shanghai. The experts were unwilling to sell at a loss due to the high cost, so they did not show samples after arrival, waiting for a good price to sell again. However, the news of the import has been rumored in the market, and those who asked about foreign rice were watching and unmoved. Xiaowen rice should have risen by 1-2 jiao yesterday, but because of this news, the rising trend was immediately frustrated. The whole city opened 600 bags of Chen Xiaowen, which were purchased by the Ningbo Trade, and the price was 8.68 yuan, which was softer than the previous market. It has been affected by the new arrival of Saigon.
